What I Saw and Heard on a Trip to the West 62

— Ji Yuan

Record of a Visit to Beibei (Part 2)

4. The Western China Science Institute: The institute was established in the autumn of 1930 and was founded single-handedly by Mr. Lu Zuofu. A board of directors was formed, with Mr. Liu Xiang, the current chairman of the Sichuan Provincial Government, as chairman, and Mr. Lu Zuofu as president. The institute has four research institutes: biology, physics and chemistry, agriculture and forestry, and geology. The Biology Institute has a botanical garden and a zoo. The botanical garden has more than one hundred species of fruit seedlings, totaling more than six thousand plants. The nursery covers an area of about twenty acres and has more than one hundred species of forest seedlings, totaling more than three hundred thousand plants. There are more than eight thousand bulbs of the lily family, orchid family, and bulbous plants. The zoo has dozens of species such as bears, tigers, leopards, and foxes. There were originally two leopards, each eating five catties of beef a day. Now, for the sake of saving provincial expenses, one is kept, and the other was shot and made into a specimen, which is displayed in the museum, all of which are located in the Civilian Park. Many people visit every day. The main research work of the institute is to collect animal, plant, and insect specimens from various provinces in western China, totaling 11,799 plant specimens with more than 50,000 copies, and 5,740 plant specimens from various provinces and regions of China exchanged from various research institutions. There are a total of 2,260 animal specimens and more than 30,000 insect specimens.

The main work of the Institute of Physics and Chemistry is to collect and solicit samples of minerals and industrial raw materials from various places for chemical testing. In the past, it has collected 258 kinds of coal mines from the Jialing River and the border areas of eastern Sichuan and western Hubei, and more than 140 kinds of other minerals for chemical testing, and compiled a general report on coal chemical testing, which is listed as one of the institute's publications.

The Institute of Agriculture and Forestry is located in Shangba, Dongyang Town, Jiangbei, and has two agricultural farms, one in Dongyang Town, covering an area of 116 acres, and one in Xishanping, covering an area of more than 2,500 acres, which was reclaimed from wasteland. It is said that the Dongyang Town agricultural farm is used for vegetable, horticulture, fruit tree breeding, and crop testing. The Xishanping agricultural farm is used for forestry, fruit trees, crops, and animal husbandry. Unfortunately, due to rain, I was unable to visit.

The Geological Institute was formally established in 1932. The main task is to investigate the geology of Sichuan Province. The counties that have been investigated are Jiangbei, Linyong, Dazhu, Qu County, Guang'an, Hechuan, Tongnan, Tongliang, Bishan, and Yongchuan. The Geology of the Area between Chongqing and Nanchuan and the Geology of the Three Gorges of the Jialing River in Sichuan have been compiled and published.

In addition to the above four major research projects, there are three affiliated projects: (1) Museum, (2) Public Library, (3) Jianshan School. The museum is located in Beibei Civilian Park and was formally established in 1930. It is divided into two parts: the exhibition room and the zoo, and also has an affiliated Hechuan Science Museum. The regular monthly expenses are about 400 yuan. The exhibition room is divided into sections for local customs, hygiene, coal mines, products of the Three Gorges area, currency, and industrial arts, and is located in Beibei Civilian Park, local hospitals, Hechuan Science Museum, and various tea houses in Beibei City. There are more than 3,490 exhibits and more than 1,000 landscape photos from various places. Among them, the local customs exhibition room is the most valuable for research, especially the customs of Xikang, most of which were collected by the museum staff who went to Xikang in person. There are many Buddhist statues from Xikang on display. According to people in the museum, people in Xikang are very devout Buddhists and must offer food to the Buddha at every meal, and they carry Buddhist statues with them. Also, most people in Xikang are illiterate. The "horse cards" used by the government (similar to the documents currently in use), such as ordering local officials to supply cattle and horses, will draw several heads of cattle and several heads of horses on the horse card, and the local officials will allocate them accordingly. The zoo is located in the Civilian Park for public viewing. The public library has more than 16,000 books, more than 140 kinds of magazines, and more than 20 kinds of newspapers. There is a reading room, four reference rooms, a special research collection room, and four modern knowledge exhibitions. Among them, the modern knowledge exhibition is the most eye-catching, because it uses pictures and simple literature to show the audience where China's weaknesses lie.

Jianshan School was also founded in 1930 and is divided into junior high school and elementary school. There are about 200 students. Although the environment is good, it is difficult to develop due to financial difficulties.

5. The Three Gorges Dyeing and Weaving Factory: The economic construction projects in Beibei District include the Three Gorges Dyeing and Weaving Factory, the Beichuan Railway Company, the Tianfu Coal Mine Company, the Qiyuan Coal Mine Company, the Suichuan Coal Mine Company, the Jialing Coal Ball Factory, the Huoxu Cave Hydroelectric Plant, the Natural Battery Factory, the Fuyuan Hydroelectric Plant, the Jingangbei Steelmaking Plant, the Fuhua Iron Factory, the Sheng Jingzhi Iron Factory, the Huili Match Factory, the Hongji Ice Factory, and the Lihua Glass Factory. Except for the Three Gorges Dyeing and Weaving Factory and the Tianfu Coal Mine Company, the rest are very small in scale. Some have a capital of only 5,000 yuan. Most coal mines are also mined using old methods. Due to time constraints, the reporter only visited the Three Gorges Dyeing and Weaving Factory, the Beichuan Railway, the Tianfu Coal Mine Company, and the Jialing Coal Ball Factory. The Three Gorges Dyeing and Weaving Factory is near the Gorges Defense Bureau. It originally belonged to the Gorges Defense Bureau and was reorganized and independent in the autumn of 1930. The factory has fixed assets of 109,300 yuan and current assets of 87,000 yuan. It has four departments: power, sizing and bleaching, reeling, and weaving. There are 106 male workers and 84 female workers. One part is still woven with hand-operated machines. The products include various colors of Gorges wool, Luo Fu wool, Freedom wool, Zhongshan wool, stuffed wool, towel cloth, honeycomb cloth, etc., which are sold in Chongqing, Chengdu, Xufu, Luzhou, Guang'an, Shunqing, Hechuan, Beibei, and other places. The prices are more expensive than those produced by various factories in Shanghai. The average working hours for workers are about 12 hours per day, and the wages range from one dime to three dimes. The air circulation inside is still hygienic.

6. Beichuan Railway: The Beichuan Railway is the only light railway in Sichuan. The entire line is more than thirty miles long. Construction began in 1928, and the section from Shuilan'e to Tudi'e began operation in October 1929. The entire project was presided over by Danish engineer Mr. Shou Erz. The starting point of the railway is built on the cliffs by the Jialing River. When passing by boat, you can sometimes hear the sound of the whistle. If you look up from the boat, you can see a train winding through the sky. If you look down from the car, you will see that there is no land below, which makes people feel uneasy. The reporter took the Beichuan Railway train back and forth once and saw that the track laying was narrower than the ordinary railway and the car traveled quite slowly, and the bumps were more severe than ordinary passenger cars. Because the railway is a light railway, its main purpose of construction is to transport coal. The annual surplus is more than 17,000 yuan.

7. Tianfu Coal Mine Company: It is said that the company was formed by merging several old small factories. The current capital is 240,000 yuan, part of which is the factory price of the old factories merged, and part of which is newly raised capital. The mining area is about fifteen miles, and the mining areas from Maliuwan to Daijiagou are all owned by the company. According to Engineer Min of the company, the company is still using indigenous methods for mining and the sales are not wide, so it is still losing money. The company originally had six factories, but only four are still operating. The reasons are (1) supply exceeds demand, (2) the production cost of the other two factories is too high. The company's coal area can be divided into two types: (1) Permian, growing in limestone cliffs, the thickest coal seam reaches 15 feet, which can be used for coking (the coal produced in the entire Sichuan Province, only Jiangbei, Nanchuan, and Peng County can be coked), but the quality of Permian coal is not good and cannot be used for ships, (2) Jurassic, which is everywhere, the thickest coal seam is about one and a half feet, produced in sandstone cliffs, and the quality is very good. Currently, the company can produce 300 tons of coal per day. The price per ton is six yuan for foamy lump coal, five yuan for hard lump coal, four yuan for foamy coal, and three yuan and five dimes for hard coal. But the above is only the price at the Baimiaozi station. Each ton needs to add about eight yuan for transportation fees. The company has more than 300 direct workers, and about 2,000 people including indirect workers. In addition to Tianfu Coal Mine, there is also the Sancai Shenggu Joint Stock Company in Baimiaozi Coal Mine. The organization is very old-fashioned, with a capital of 200,000, and it is also losing money. The reason is also that the mining method is poor and the transportation cost is too high. Now, we can only try our best to tighten our belts in order to survive.

The reporter stayed in Beibei and Wenquan Park for four days. What I saw and heard made me feel that the spirit of autonomy and talent training in Beibei District are quite worthy of being a mirror for rural construction in other provinces. However, the modernization of production methods is what Beibei and even the entire Sichuan Province urgently need to pursue.

Repairs to Collapsed Dikes of the Yangtze and Han Rivers to Commence Within the Month 63

Construction plans have been reviewed and approved, and large sums of money have been allocated. The main dikes will use labor relief, and the people's dikes will use compulsory labor.

A Hankou dispatch states that the authorities have been planning to repair the collapsed dikes of the Yangtze and Han Rivers for some time, but work has not yet begun. Not only is the dry winter season passing, but the disaster victims who are eagerly awaiting work relief are also crying for hunger and cold, which is too late to remedy. It was found that after the flood occurred, a joint meeting was held on August 2 by four agencies: the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Construction, the Flood Relief Association, and the Yangtze-Han Engineering Bureau to discuss the dike repair methods and decided on two principles: (1) Recruit refugees in the disaster-stricken areas for work relief; (2) In areas with autumn harvests, conscript labor for embankment repair according to the people's compulsory labor method, and divide responsibilities. The investigation and statistics of the dikes and embankments in the province will be handled by the Department of Construction in conjunction with the Yangtze-Han Engineering Bureau. The embankment repair, inspection, and rectification will be fully responsible by the Yangtze-Han Engineering Bureau. The authorities' steps were consistent, and the planning was not too early. However, the degree of damage to dikes and embankments in various places exceeded that of the past twenty years, and the scale of the project was also incomparable to that of the past twenty years. The central government's relief funds are less than those of the past twenty years, and the approved construction funds have not been allocated for a long time, which has delayed the start of construction. This is the biggest reason. Secondly, the large number of collapsed dikes, which ones should be repaired by the government, which ones should be repaired by the people, which ones should be repaired, and which ones should be abandoned, and the issues of which should be repaired first and which should be repaired later, also need to be thoroughly investigated and carefully designed, which is also one of the reasons for the delayed start of construction. After taking office, Xi Dejiong, Director of the Yangtze-Han Engineering Bureau, immediately convened a meeting of the heads of various engineering offices and engineers to discuss and determine the construction plan. Pu Deli, a consultant from the Water Conservancy Department of the Economic Commission, and Section Chief Wang Hu came to Hankou to review and approve it. Because the funds needed were too large, Xi took the plan to the capital for instructions. Recently, the Economic Commission decided to implement it. The content of the plan focuses on repairing the collapsed openings, followed by repairs. In terms of the main dikes alone, a total of more than 6 million yuan is needed for labor and materials. The collapsed openings of the Xiang River Third and Fourth Works dikes require more than 2 million yuan, and the Eleventh Works and other collapsed openings require more than 3 million yuan. In addition to the provincial dike engineering funds, which can cover 2 million yuan, the Economic Commission has approved the allocation of 2 million yuan. The remaining 2 million yuan will be requested from the central government to be allocated from the Hubei Province work relief funds. Since the funds have been raised, construction is not very difficult. Shi Yuling, the Sixth District Administrative Commissioner, has recruited 100,000 civilians to be responsible for repairing the collapsed openings of the Third and Fourth Works dikes and the remote dikes. The food is also prepared by the Flood Relief Association. It is expected to officially start construction within this month. For the people's dikes, there are a total of 36 counties with dikes, and the number of dikes and embankments is uncertain. According to the results of the current investigation by dispatched personnel, the number is dozens for the small ones and hundreds for the large ones. The number can be said to be alarming. This year's flood was huge, and none of them survived. At least 10 million yuan is needed for repairs. Generally, the people will be responsible for the repairs through compulsory labor, supplemented by work relief. The required food expenses will also be covered. Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Provincial Government, has repeatedly requested assistance from the central government in the capital and has reportedly been approved. Therefore, the construction of the people's dikes will be carried out simultaneously with the main dikes and will be completed before May next year. (15th)

The Nature of League of Nations Sanctions 64

— Ang Ruo

If there are no other changes, the economic sanctions imposed by the League of Nations on Italy will begin to be implemented on the 18th of this month. This is an unprecedented move since the establishment of the League of Nations on January 16, 1920, and also a precedent for collective action to punish warmongers. However, the issue of sanctions is very complex and has led to misunderstandings among the general public. The nature of sanctions and the legal basis for their implementation are analyzed below.

"Sanction" is a legal term, meaning to force lawbreakers to obey the law. The spirit of the law lies in the use of public power to implement sanctions after proper inquiry, and not by arbitrary enforcement by one person. The difference between this rule of law in the international sphere and within a nation lies in the absence of a strict legal code like national law in the international sphere. In the international arena, since 1920, the meaning of the rule of law has been twofold: (1) to abide by international treaties, and (2) to resolve any disputes between friendly nations through agreement or other legal procedures, rather than resorting to war. These principles are enshrined in the Covenant of the League of Nations, and member states that sign the Covenant have the responsibility to implement these principles.

But in addition to stating these principles, the Covenant also contains more advanced provisions. Articles 10, 11, 13(4), 15(6, 7), and 16 of the Covenant stipulate the measures the League of Nations should take to prevent those who intend to or actually violate the Covenant.

Article 10 stipulates that "The Members of the League undertake to respect and preserve as against external aggression the territorial integrity and existing political independence of all Members of the League. In case of any such aggression or in case of any threat or danger of such aggression the Council shall advise upon the means by which this obligation shall be fulfilled." This is a general article applicable to threats of aggression and actual aggression. The specific methods to be adopted for any particular case shall be planned by the Council. There is nothing to prevent the Council from recommending the adoption of some or all of the sanctions stipulated in Article 16. However, in the absence of other express provisions regarding this article and other articles (such as Article 15(6, 7) and Article 16), the resolutions of the Council of the League of Nations must be unanimous.

Article 16 stipulates the methods for implementing sanctions against warmongers. The condition for implementation is that a country "resorts to war in disregard of its covenants under Articles 12, 13 or 15, it shall ipso facto be deemed to have committed an act of war against all other Members of the League, which hereby undertake immediately to subject it to" expressly stated sanctions. However, in order to implement Article 16, war must have actually broken out.

Articles 10 and 11 allow for action to be taken in the event of a danger of war or when war has already broken out, without any expressly stipulated measures. Article 10 has already been discussed. Article 11 declares that any war or danger of war is a matter of concern to the entire league. "The League shall take any action that may be deemed wise and effectual to safeguard the peace of nations." The wording is very broad. The Legal Section of the Thirteenth Committee, in its report, cited the opinion of the Council Committee of 1927, "allowing the adoption of any measures other than war to deal with recalcitrant states." According to the Legal Section's opinion, any measures adopted under this article should be of a preventive nature. Furthermore, in the absence of specific agreements, states are not legally obliged to comply with the Council's recommendations. The measures in this article differ from those in Article 16, which stipulates that sanctions should be imposed on a state that resorts to war in violation of the Covenant.

According to Article 13(4), if the Council encounters a state that fails to implement a judgment, "the Council shall propose what steps should be taken to give effect thereto." According to the Legal Section's opinion, any measures implemented under this article must be limited to achieving this objective.

Article 15(6, 7) stipulates passive sanctions, which means that if the Council's report, excluding the representative(s) of one or more of the parties to the dispute, is unanimously approved by the members of the Council, then the members of the League agree "that they will not go to war with any party to the dispute which complies with the recommendations of the report."

Before studying the difficult issues of interpreting and implementing sanctions, the nature of the various sanctions should be analyzed. Sanctions can be divided into four categories: (1) moral and diplomatic measures, (2) financial and economic measures, (3) international boycotts, and (4) military measures. There is an important divide between the above four types of sanctions, namely, that the first two types of measures against the violating country will not involve combat, but if the violating country actively resists the latter two types of measures, it will inevitably lead to war. This point will be examined in more detail later.

Public opinion is one type of moral sanction, and it is bound to exert considerable power. Public opinion within the aggressor country may be deceived by government propaganda, but the unanimous global opposition to the aggressor country cannot be completely ignored. Credit depends on trust, and trust can be undermined by foreign criticism. But public opinion is difficult to be effective without concrete actions to back it up. Concrete actions can be expressed through diplomatic channels, such as warnings, protests, withdrawal of diplomatic representatives, and severance of diplomatic relations. These measures have both advantages and disadvantages. There is also the measure of non-recognition (such as the note to Japan by US Secretary of State Stimson on January 7, 1932 regarding the Manchurian problem, and the resolution passed by the General Assembly of the League of Nations on March 11 of the same year).

The second category of financial and economic sanctions varies in severity. Financial sanctions come in three forms: stopping long-term loans, short-term bank credit loans, and commercial credit accounts. Financial sanctions, when implemented in a timely manner, can be effective and easy to implement, without a broad impact on the implementing countries, but they also have weaknesses. The sanctioned country can use it to cancel foreign debts as retaliation. In addition, there are measures to provide financial assistance to the aggressed country. The Financial Assistance Convention was established in 1930 (signed by 30 countries, including the United Kingdom, Belgium, France, Germany, Italy, Poland, Spain, the Little Entente countries, and the Scandinavian countries), but it has not yet been implemented. If this convention were effective, the aggressed country would have the opportunity to obtain financial assistance from other members of the League of Nations, and the aggressor country would have to think twice before acting.

Before discussing economic sanctions, the distinction between passive and challenging measures should be made. The League of Nations can recommend prohibiting the export of military supplies and strategic raw materials. All member states can unanimously agree to implement the prohibition within their own countries. However, if the military supply producing countries that are not members of the League of Nations do not act in concert, the prohibition cannot be thorough. In this case, the League of Nations has to decide whether to implement a blockade, and if the aggressor country wants to break through this blockade, it will inevitably lead to war, and even disputes with non-member states are possible.

However, there are many measures that can be taken before implementing the harsh measure of a blockade. The unanimous boycott of goods from the aggressor country by many countries can have a significant impact. It is easier to implement a ban on imports in the sanctioning countries than a ban on exports. In terms of administration, it is easier to verify the origin of goods than to verify the destination. It can be done without a blockade, and its power is sufficient to deprive the aggressor country of foreign exchange—this loss in itself is very serious and can hinder the aggressor country from purchasing goods from other sources.

As for the prohibition of exports, the most important thing to implement is of course weapons, ammunition, and military supplies. There are considerable difficulties in implementation. First, it has always been difficult to agree on who is the true warmonger, which is also the crux of the entire sanction issue. Second, there have always been different opinions on whether the two parties in conflict should be prohibited from exporting at the same time. For example, in the Sino-Japanese issue, the United Kingdom initiated a joint ban on both parties, but other countries did not agree, and the ban was lifted after only two weeks. In the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, some countries banned both parties. After the General Assembly of the League of Nations passed the resolution on sanctions against Italy on October 9, 50 member states had lifted the ban on Ethiopia.

Whether the prohibition of military supplies is effective depends entirely on whether the sanctioned country is a producer, and whether the prohibition has loopholes. The attitude of producing countries that are not members of the League of Nations is also very important. For producing and highly industrialized countries, it is only effective to prohibit key raw materials at the same time. However, countries that deliberately commit aggression must have stockpiled these types of raw materials long ago. However, in the current era of increasing specialization and mechanization, a country's military strength is also increasingly dependent on various commodities. Therefore, the effectiveness of economic sanctions is also considerable.

Now, let us study the sanctions stipulated in Article 16 of the Covenant, namely the international boycott in Article 16(1) and the military sanctions in Articles 16(2, 3). The interpretation of this article will be discussed later. Now, let us first study its measures. The most important point to note is that Article 16 can only be implemented after a country has disregarded the Covenant and resorted to war.

In this case, "it shall ipso facto be deemed to have committed an act of war against all other Members of the League, which hereby undertake immediately to subject it to the severance of all trade or financial relations, the prohibition of all intercourse between their nationals and the nationals of the covenant-breaking State, and the prevention of all financial, commercial or personal intercourse between the nationals of the covenant-breaking State and the nationals of any other State, whether a Member of the League or not."

If the international boycott can be universally implemented in accordance with the original intentions of the drafters of the Covenant, it will definitely be effective. If the sanctioned country resists, and all countries are prepared to back it up with blockades or military action, the effectiveness will be even greater. In this regard, the major powers that are not members of the League of Nations are in a very important position. Even if all members of the League of Nations unanimously implement the international boycott, it is not without doubt. The extent to which countries rely on foreign trade varies, and the impact of this boycott also varies accordingly. Moreover, it is generally believed that no country can be immune to the damage of a thorough boycott.

In order for a boycott to be completely effective, it must be able to completely close the border, sever all postal, telegraphic, shipping, and aviation links, withdraw all consular personnel, and even detain or repatriate the nationals of the boycotted country.

The implementation of these measures will inevitably raise a number of questions. The resistance of the sanctioned country to the blockade will inevitably lead to military action and combat measures. The attitude of non-member states of the League of Nations must be considered. In addition, neighboring countries, especially small and weak countries, will be in a very difficult situation, and special measures must be taken to protect their status, so that they are exempted from participating in the boycott or protect their national defense. There is also the issue of compensation. The damage caused by the boycott varies, and countries with less damage should compensate countries with more damage. In this regard, Article 16(3) stipulates that "The Members of the League agree, further, that they will mutually support one another in the financial and economic measures which are taken under this Article, in order to minimise the loss and inconvenience resulting therefrom."

Article 16(2) stipulates that "It shall be the duty of the Council in such case to recommend to the several governments concerned what effective military, naval or air force the Members of the League shall severally contribute to the armed forces to be used to protect the covenants of the League." According to paragraph 3, the members of the League also agree that "they will take the necessary steps to afford passage through their territory to the forces of any of the Members of the League which are co-operating to protect the covenants of the League."

In practice, how military measures are to be implemented is not expressly stipulated. In some cases, the Council of the League of Nations may designate one or more countries to take military, naval, and air force action. The Council may also recommend that member states send troops to form a League of Nations army. The voluntary recruitment of this international army will inevitably delay the timing, and the designation of the supreme command is also a difficult issue. The League of Nations' hosting of the formation of an international peacekeeping force has been initiated by several countries, but it is still far from being mature.

Therefore, military sanction measures must be determined according to the specific circumstances of each case, and the geographical environment is a particularly important factor. In practice, some countries will not be limited to the provisions of Article 16 of the Covenant, and will inevitably be drawn into the vortex of war, and will have to do their best to deal with it.

The implementation of Article 16 and the rights and obligations of member states of the League of Nations have raised important questions of interpretation. In this regard, the opinions of jurists are often inconsistent. However, the resolutions passed by the Second General Assembly of the League of Nations in October 1921 can serve as a basis. The first resolution stipulates that "It is for the government of each Member to decide whether a breach of the Covenant has been committed," which means that the implementation of Article 16 is automatic, that is, if a country disregards the Covenant and resorts to war, and each member state of the League of Nations has determined this fact on its own, the member state has a responsibility to take military action, but this responsibility is not mandatory. The fourth resolution states that "The Members of the League are bound to take the necessary measures to carry out the obligations which devolve upon them in virtue of this Article; any omission is tantamount to a breach of the Covenant." However, if a country has decided that the Covenant has not been breached, the recommendations of the Council of the League of Nations are invalid, and the country cannot be forced to implement sanctions.

The fifth resolution stipulates that any case of breach of the Covenant under Article 16 "shall be brought before the Council as a matter of urgency at the request of any Member of the League." The Secretary-General shall immediately notify all members of the Council, convene a meeting as soon as possible to study the case, and make recommendations. If the Council considers that the Covenant has been breached, then according to the sixth resolution, the minutes shall be submitted to all members of the League of Nations, together with a written explanation and a notice of action to be taken. Other resolutions stipulate that the Council may form a committee of experts to assist in the handling of the matter, and the Council shall recommend the date on which the economic sanctions of Article 16 should begin to be implemented, and shall be responsible for notifying all members. If the economic sanctions are extended, then gradual and more stringent measures must be taken, and the prohibition of food supply is the last step, and efforts must be made to ensure the cooperation of countries that are not members of the League of Nations.

The importance of these resolutions lies in the clear stipulation that they do not interfere with national sovereignty, that the sanction action is joint, not individual, and that the measures stipulated in Article 16 do not have to be implemented immediately and simultaneously, but can be implemented in stages.

Regarding the interpretation of economic sanctions, experts still have a different point of view. One side believes that the economic sanctions of Article 16 must be a complete boycott of the breaching country and its people. This boycott must be passive, and all countries are limited to stopping all interactions. But it must also be active, and all countries should actively prohibit the breaching country from interacting with any member state and non-member state.

The other side believes that, based on the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the economic sanctions stipulated in Article 16 only require each member state to implement them within its own territory. Member states of the League of Nations are not responsible for taking action outside their own borders and implementing a blockade. However, in this regard, it is very clear that the boycott can only be effective if all countries can implement it within their own territory.

The key to the success of sanctions lies in the concentration of all the strength of the League of Nations members to deal with the aggressor country. The drafters of the Covenant thought that the League of Nations was a worldwide organization, and that the power of the whole world to deal with an aggressor country would surely make it yield. However, as British Foreign Secretary Hoare stated in Geneva on September 11, the League of Nations has lacked several major powers as members from the beginning, and other countries have since withdrawn. However, the responsibilities of the Covenant still exist, and the burden on the countries that remain in the League of Nations has greatly increased as a result.

The situation of the League of Nations General Assembly passing sanctions against Italy.

The Qiantang River Bridge at Yingkou 65

— Zhang Changren

Having visited Hangzhou and traveled in the lakes and mountains for two days, I went to admire the Temple of Yue Fei, and visited the many scenic spots of Lingyin and Taoguang. Following the mountain road behind Longjing Temple, I twisted and turned to explore the Nine Streams and Eighteen Gorges. Although the camellias were old, the pines and bamboos remained the same, the verdant color assaulted the senses, and my face felt refreshed. The quiet mountain road, the stream water, sometimes passed through stones and over paths, murmuring under my feet... it was like being in a painting. When I arrived at the Jiuxi Tea Plantation, I originally planned to pass through Yangmeiling Manjuelong to peek at the Shuile Cave, Yanhua Cave, and Stone House Cave. However, I heard that the Qiantang River Bridge was under major construction, with the goal of completing it in the shortest possible time, in order to connect the traffic of the two Zhejiang provinces, so I changed course and went bravely. The north end of the Qiantang River Bridge is located between Zhakou and the Liuhe Pagoda. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway extends here and stops. The Hangzhou-Fuyang Highway starts from here and goes west along the river. Once completed, it will have special value in both commerce and national defense.

Because of the construction of the bridge, this once desolate riverside has been transformed into a small industrial area. Building materials are everywhere, and there are no less than a hundred tall and complete workshops. The voices of workers shouting and the sound of machinery operating are mixed together. The riverside revetment has been built, and three or five bridge piers for the approach bridge have also been completed. They are tall and solid, unlike anything I have seen before. There is a temporary bridge about a hundred feet long on the embankment, to reach the first bridge pier in the river, which is more than half built. Light railways are laid on it, and the workers' access and the transportation of materials all rely on it. The construction of this temporary bridge is also not easy, and it will gradually extend from both banks to the center of the river as the bridge piers are built one by one.

According to Mr. Sun Baochu, one of the Chinese engineers, the construction of this bridge started with a groundbreaking ceremony on November 11 last year. The Danish company Kang Yiyang, to which he belongs, contracted to build the bridge piers. The total construction cost is about 5 million yuan. In February of this year, the foreign company began to transport the means of production and building materials one after another, and started work. It was originally scheduled to be completed in one year, but unfortunately, due to the floods, the entire embankment project that had been completed was destroyed. The reconstruction began in February. There are currently more than a thousand workers working, and it is planned to add more people later. However, it will not be possible to complete it by this time next year—early November.

The bridge is about 5,000 feet long, with a net length of 3,520 feet. There are 15 bridge piers, divided into 16 spans, each span 220 feet. There are approach bridges at both ends, totaling more than 1,000 feet. The bridge body is divided into two layers. The lower layer is used to lay the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, and the upper layer is the highway. The net width of the bridge body is 17 feet, with 5-foot sidewalks on both sides of the upper layer. The center distance between the two beams is 20 feet.

The depth of the Qiantang River at this point is about 70 feet at the shallowest point, and the lowest point is 150 to 160 feet below the Wusong zero point. The water surface rises and falls by 15 feet due to the tide. The riverbed is sandy and undulating. Generally speaking, the stone layer in the north is higher than in the south. Among the 15 bridge piers, the six northern ones can be directly dug and placed on the stone layer at the bottom of the river. The other nine piers, because the riverbed is too muddy, use the pneumatic caisson method to establish the bridge piers on wooden piles or stone layers about 100 feet below the erosion line at the bottom of the river. All bridge piers are currently using this method.

Using the pneumatic caisson method to build bridge piers is the first time in China. The caisson has only five sides, 58 feet long, 37 feet wide, and 20 feet high, all made of reinforced concrete. During construction, after the cofferdam is built, the caisson is first placed on the riverbed, and then an elliptical reinforced concrete pier column is built on it. The top of the caisson has inlet and outlet holes, and the steam pipes from the three air compressors on the shore pass through these holes to enter the caisson, in order to input high-pressure air to prevent mud and water from entering, and to prevent the caisson from sinking immediately. The workers then carry out excavation work in the caisson. From then on, as the sand and soil at the bottom of the caisson are gradually removed, the caisson also gradually lowers due to the increase in air pressure, until it reaches the wooden piles or stone layers at the bottom of the river. At the same time, the pier column built on the caisson is also gradually built up, making it rise above the water surface. The steel beams of the bridge are then erected on it.

At present, the construction of the first pier in the north is more than half completed. The air pressure initially used in the caisson was only 17 to 18 pounds (4 pounds higher than atmospheric pressure), and 2 English cubic yards of sand and soil could be excavated per day. The caisson sank about 2 to 3 inches. Now the air pressure has been increased to more than 30 pounds, and the amount of sand and soil excavated per day has increased more than five times compared to before. The caisson sank about 6 to 7 inches. On the pier column standing above the water surface, it is marked that it has entered the water for more than 40 feet. Before the first pier is completed, the work on the second pier has already begun.

When the Qiantang River Bridge is completed, a large park will be established along the Qiantang River at the north end of the bridge. This double-layer iron bridge will span across it. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway train will wind its way from Nanxing Bridge across the Qiantang River to the Huangtushan on the north bank, roaring down across the river, and disappearing into the wilderness of Xiaoshan County on the opposite bank. Southbound cars will also drive across the upper layer of this bridge and enter the avenue built on the mountainside along the river, reaching Hangzhou to the north, Zhakou to the east, and Fuyang and other places to the west under the towering Liuhe Pagoda in the forest. If we can come here in the morning and evening, wandering and overlooking on the upper layer of the bridge, we can see the river winding from the west, flowing east under the bridge into the vast clouds and water. Along the river on the north bank, the peaks and mountains are verdant and blue, the highways are crisscrossing, and cars are speeding halfway up the mountain. The Liuhe Pagoda is towering and overlooking in the sunshine, and the scenery is also enough to make people feel happy.

Stabilizing the Financial Situation in Anhui Province and Anqing City 66

Establishing a Price Assessment Committee and Setting Minimum Standards for Copper Coins

Anqing Correspondence: The financial situation in Anhui has always been extremely depleted. The only things that can be used for circulation are silver coins and copper coins. Most commodity prices are based on copper coins. Each silver coin could be exchanged for 360 to 370 copper coins, depending on the price. Recently, since the Ministry of Finance implemented its currency policy, unscrupulous merchants and market vendors have taken the opportunity to hoard and manipulate prices, and transport large quantities of copper coins out of the province, resulting in a daily decrease in the number of copper coins in the market. Each silver coin is only worth about 300 copper coins, and there is an upward trend, while various daily necessities are gradually becoming more expensive, which has a huge impact on the livelihood of the common people. Therefore, the provincial government specially convened the heads of the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Bureaus, as well as the Anqing Public Security Bureau, the Huaining County Government, and the Huaining County Chamber of Commerce, at 4:00 PM on the 12th in the Civil Affairs Bureau to discuss measures to crack down on and provide relief. The following key points were resolved: (1) Establish a Price Assessment Committee in Anqing City. The detailed rules will be drafted by the Construction Bureau and submitted to the meeting for review. (2) The price of copper coins will be set at 320 coins per yuan of national currency. The Anqing Public Security Bureau will pay close attention to the outflow of copper coins and will not allow hoarding or manipulation. (3) Investigate the comparison of various daily commodity prices after the implementation of the legal tender with those before the implementation. This investigation will be carried out by the provincial government ordering the Huaining County Government and the Anqing Public Security Bureau to cooperate with the Huaining County Chamber of Commerce, and the results of the investigation will be reported in a list. On the 14th, the Huaining County Government and the Anqing Public Security Bureau have followed the orders of the provincial government and jointly issued a notice, strictly prohibiting the private transportation of copper coins out of the province, and clearly stipulating the standard market price of copper coins, with a minimum exchange rate of 320 copper coins per silver dollar, in order to gradually stabilize the financial situation in the market. (November 15)

Banking Circles in Jiangxi Province: 67

Dismantling Loans to Maintain the Qian Industry 68

Already Dismantled 300,000 Legal Tender Dollars,

Market Still Stagnant and Turnover Remains Difficult

Nanchang Correspondence: Since Jiangxi Province officially implemented the use of legal tender, the market has remained relatively stable. Due to the economic stagnation and financial exhaustion in recent years, all industries have been in extreme decline. Therefore, the impact has been minimal. Taking the Qian industry as an example, in the past two years, due to active business and frequent transactions, they made profits without losses. Now, they are in a precarious state and require banks to maintain them. The reasons are: (1) There are more than 70 Qian shops in the city. Except for a few, such as Yichangren, the capital of each shop is only between 10,000 and 50,000 yuan. However, it is not enough to do a 200,000 yuan business to cover expenses. The support of the business relies entirely on absorbing ordinary deposits and daily retail and wholesale goods payments from various industries. At this time of total social and economic collapse, there are very few funds available for deposit, and various industries also have no cash to store due to sluggish business. (2) Bankruptcies have occurred repeatedly in the city this year, and all sectors are wary of depositing and lending funds. It is difficult for the Qian industry to both deposit and lend, losing its circulation function. (3) Since the bandit disasters in the province, transactions with other counties and the turnover of import and export businesses have been extremely poor. (4) The dismantling interest rate is too high, consistently above 50%, easily resulting in bad debts. (5) Exchange and larger businesses have been completely taken over by banks. Due to these reasons, the Qian industry has been declining daily. After the implementation of legal tender, depositors rushed to withdraw their deposits, and the loans released to various industries could not be recovered. (Businesses with weak foundations cannot repay the loans, while those with solid foundations hope for inventory price increases). The Qian industry is caught in this double squeeze. On the 5th and 6th of this month, they dared not open for business. On the 7th, after Finance Director Wu discussed with the Provincial Yumin Bank, as well as the Central, China, and Transportation Banks, 300,000 legal tender dollars were dismantled and given to the members of the Qian Industry Association, which broke the deadlock. However, this 300,000 yuan is like a drop in the bucket. Each Qian shop can only handle retail and small withdrawals. It is not easy to withdraw amounts over 1,000 yuan. As for lending, it has already been stopped. The Qian Industry Association and the Exchange Association have been requesting Finance Director Wu for days to have the banking sector dismantle as much legal tender as possible to maintain the industry and facilitate turnover. The Finance Office believes that the Qian industry is the hub of all industries and is anxiously considering how to get through the New Year and next year's opening period. However, with the difficulty of turnover in various industries, there are likely to be many businesses closing down for the New Year. (November 12th)

Soaring Prices in Jiaodong 69

—Certain Foreigners Secretly Buying Up Silver Dollars—

Qingdao Correspondence: Since the central government implemented the new currency system policy, the general merchants and people do not understand the situation, resulting in widespread rumors and soaring prices, which greatly affects the people's livelihood. Even the prices of copper coins in various places have risen sharply. In Qingdao, 540 copper coins were previously exchanged for one silver dollar, but now only 380 copper coins are needed to exchange for one silver dollar. The municipal government, in order to stabilize the market and people's hearts, and to maintain local order, (1) posted notices stipulating that 500 copper coins should be exchanged for one legal tender dollar, and (2) tried to stabilize prices and prevent deliberate price increases. People's hearts gradually stabilized. However, in the Jiaodong area, such as Zhucheng, Anqiu, Gaomi, Jiaoxian, Jimo, and Yexian counties, prices are still soaring. These counties are close to Qingdao, and the prices of various goods in Qingdao are inevitably affected. In the Jiaodong counties, each dou of wheat used to be worth 3.4 yuan, but now it has risen to over 4 yuan. Each dou of beans used to be worth 3.2 yuan, but now it has risen to around 4 yuan. Each piece of cotton yarn used to be worth 160 yuan, but now it has risen to 176 yuan. Other grains and daily necessities are also soaring in price, causing panic among the people. It is also heard that certain foreigners have secretly sent people to various counties in Jiaodong to buy up silver dollars at high prices. Initially, they used 1.3 legal tender dollars to buy one silver dollar, but now they are using 1.5 legal tender dollars to buy one silver dollar. Therefore, merchants and people who have silver dollars are regarding them as rare commodities, and many unscrupulous merchants are happy to buy them for the foreigners, hoping to profit from it. This is also one of the reasons for the soaring prices.

Political and Police Opium Case Sent to the Province for Review 71

Zhang Yingze, Ke Jun, Huang Zhongfu, Gong Jinyun, Yang Lisheng, Fei Yongxing, and other six political and police officers of the county government were reported in December of the 23rd year for smoking opium. It is now learned that the county government suddenly received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs, instructing them to send the police officers to the province for re-examination, and also ordered that the director of the county opium detoxification center, Sun Youxin, be given a demerit, and the doctor Dong Zhaoteng be dismissed. Except for Huang Zhongfu and others, who fled upon hearing the news, the county sent Zhang Yingze and Ke Jun, who were detained, to the province on the 15th under police escort.

Suzhou: 72

Representatives of Chambers of Commerce and Merchant Corps in Various Counties 73

Meet to Discuss the Issue of Retention or Abolition of Merchant Corps 74

The chambers of commerce in various counties are facing the abolition of the merchant corps as ordered by the government, which coincides with the serious period of winter defense. Therefore, the chambers of commerce and merchant corps in various counties have selected representatives to hold a joint meeting at the Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce at 3 pm on the 17th to discuss the issue of retention or abolition. More than 20 representatives from more than 10 counties attended the meeting. Mr. Lu Xiaobo was elected as the temporary chairman. The chairman reported that the Zhenjiang Merchant Corps had many obligations and few employees. As for the necessity of the existence of the merchant corps, taking Zhenjiang as an example, the military and police are densely deployed, which is sufficient to maintain local security. Therefore, there is no real need for its existence. I don't know what the situation is in other counties. In my personal opinion, it seems more convenient for the county government to preside over it, with merchants participating. What should be done, please discuss together. After discussion and consultation by the representatives, it was unanimously decided to first ask Chairman Lu Xiaobo to contact Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government and Director Yu of the Department of Civil Affairs. Then, taking advantage of the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce's meeting in the provincial capital on the 21st of this month, invite the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs and the Director of the Provincial Security Office to conduct joint research at the Zhenjiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce to decide on everything. The meeting then adjourned, when the lights of ten thousand homes were already on. That night, the Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce, the Fire Fighting Federation, and the Merchant Corps Headquarters hosted a banquet for the representatives of various counties at the Yanqing Restaurant outside the Panmen Gate.

Clearing Household Registration to Eliminate Bandits 76

The county government of this county held its first winter defense meeting the day before yesterday. The chairman was the section chief. The resolutions were: 1. The total monthly expenses for the winter defense headquarters are 10 yuan, and the monthly expenses for the sub-offices are 5 yuan, which will be submitted by the county to the province for approval. 2. The county magistrate will order all districts to thoroughly clear the household registration in order to eliminate bandits. 3. Unemployed vagrants and disbanded soldiers will be accommodated as much as possible by the county magistrate's civilian vocational training center. 4. Patrol teams will be organized to thoroughly inspect hotels, teahouses, theaters, taverns, thatched huts, and awning boats in order to maintain security. 5. A request will be submitted to the county government to convene neighboring counties to hold joint defense. 6. Joint water and land defense will be discussed and jointly prevented by the Public Security Bureau and the Water Police Team.

Education Broadcast Special Issue

Central Military Academy Instructor

The Meaning and Function of Science 83

—Gan Xiangrong, Instructor, Central Military Academy

(I) What is science? The term science is the English word "Science" or the German word "Wissenschaft". If interpreted broadly, science should include the spiritual sciences (i.e., sociology, history, law, and economics, etc.) and the natural sciences. However, the science generally referred to by people is interpreted narrowly, and its content is limited to the natural sciences.

Natural science takes natural objects and natural phenomena as its research objects. Physiology, geology, astronomy, and physical chemistry are all natural sciences. As for mathematics, although it has a close relationship with natural science, mathematics does not belong to natural science in strict scientific classification.

In the 18th century, the French mathematical philosopher d'Alembert classified mathematics into the natural sciences when he edited the encyclopedia. However, later scholars such as Wundt separated mathematics from the natural sciences.

Mathematics is an abstract formal science, while natural science is an experiential material science. Their essences are mutually opposed and cannot belong to each other. Natural science studies objective experiential content, while mathematics is not bound by experience. For example, imaginary numbers or complex numbers are of little use in the calculation of experiential ordinary things, and four-dimensional or five-dimensional space is definitely not our experiential space.

The study of natural science, especially physics, must rely on mathematics. Einstein's theory of relativity succeeded with the advancement of higher numbers, but the basis of the theory of relativity lies in experiential reality and is definitely not entirely based on mathematical deduction. In other studies such as astronomy and theoretical chemistry, mathematics is an indispensable research method, but the essence of the knowledge is completely independent of mathematics. In short, natural science is an objective experiential science, while mathematics is transcendent and irrelevant to experience. The two should not be mixed together.

(II) The essence of science: Humans have two desires for nature: one is the hope to explore the mystery of nature; the other is the hope to use nature for daily life. In order to satisfy these two desires, they study natural objects and various natural phenomena from all aspects. In this way, they gradually accumulate fragments of knowledge and organize and verify them, and then gradually discover universal causal relationships, which can lead to the establishment of science. There is a very important principle in the path of establishing science. This principle is: to seek to explain facts by confirming facts. If our predetermined theory is contrary to the facts, then this theory that does not conform to the facts should be overthrown.

The above-mentioned thought of respecting facts originated in the era of Greek philosophy, and its maturity was only realized until the period of modern scientific development. How can we confirm the facts? The main methods are observation and experiment. Observation refers to the artificial attention to natural phenomena to obtain correct experience. Experiment refers to the use of artificial methods to transform complex natural phenomena into simpler ones, and then analyze them to determine the truth of the facts. All researchers of science know the importance of observation and experiment. Without precise observation and experimental methods, natural science will never progress. In other words, the methods of observation and experiment are gradually improved, and their precision is gradually increased. Thus, science can develop. Therefore, if we want to understand the essence or characteristics of science, we should first mention observation and experiment.

Still others want to understand the essence of science by examining it from its method. Let me briefly describe it. The methods of science can be divided into (1) description and classification, (2) induction of special cases into general necessary laws, and (3) recognition of purposefulness in biological phenomena. Description and classification are methods commonly used in zoology, botany, mineralogy, and many places in chemistry. Combining similar natural objects under one class concept is called "classification." Analyzing the characteristics of each class and expressing them is called "description." Description and classification must explore the essential properties of the object as the basis for classification, and the means of exploration rely on observation and experiment. Therefore, without precise observation and experiment, description or classification cannot be accurate. Establishing laws is the ultimate goal of natural science. The so-called "law" must have universality and necessity that transcend time and space. For example, Newton's law of universal gravitation in physics and Mendeleev's periodic law in chemistry are both universal necessary laws. Their establishment is based on the induction of various special experiences and verification. However, their basis is still the result of observation and experiment. Later, new facts are obtained from advanced observation and experiment, and then laws such as universal gravitation and the periodic law must be revised. As for biological phenomena, they cannot be explained purely by causal laws. Therefore, for the overall study of biology, we cannot discuss mechanical causal relationships in the same way as physics and chemistry. Biological phenomena must be viewed from the perspective of purpose and means, in addition to causal relationships. Even in Darwin's theory of evolution, the principles of "natural selection" or "survival of the fittest" do not only refer to causal relationships but also contain some teleological components. However, in any case, the study of biological phenomena is definitely not based on empty imagination. Its basis must also be in accurate observation and experiment.

In short, natural science originates from human's desire for knowledge and utilization, and the development and progress of natural science depend entirely on the accuracy of observation and experimental methods. In order to understand the essence of science, we should of course understand this principle.

(III) The influence of science on modern thought: Science has a profound influence on the thinking of modern people. Therefore, science has a close relationship with various schools of thought in modern times. Here, we will only examine the influence of science on the world of thought from the two aspects of idealism and materialism.

Idealism takes the soul as the highest argument. The most primitive and most dominant idealism of mankind is religion. In the early days of science, religion exercised its authority in faith and often oppressed science. The Roman Emperor of Christianity in Europe regarded the heliocentric theory as heresy and severely punished and interfered with it. Galileo claimed that the heliocentric theory was correct based on the observation of stars, but his book was banned, and he was ordered to swear that his statement was wrong. In the 19th century, Darwin's theory of biological evolution was also opposed by religious scholars. However, science has objective truth, and no oppression can damage it in the slightest. Therefore, the rise of science has forced religious theories to be reformed. On the one hand, there should also be reflective investigations on science itself. Science takes objective experience as its object, but what is experience? Our understanding of natural objects and natural phenomena all depends on the senses of our five senses (sight, smell, taste, hearing, touch). Then what is sensation? These questions raise reflective doubts about the "object" itself and the truth of science. Therefore, science does not destroy idealism, but adopts a critical attitude of improvement towards idealism. Pearson once said: Scientific knowledge is a synthesis of the reality of sensation plus the organization of thinking. Then it can be known that the truth of science is a natural model formed by our thinking. Nature is complete and whole, and the various divisions of natural science are just cross-sections of various aspects of the above-mentioned natural model.

Materialism takes matter as the only basis for discussion. The prosperity of natural science caused the industrial revolution, which transformed society from an agricultural society to an industrial society, and transformed life from rural life to concentrated urban life, which made modern people fascinated by materialistic thoughts. The foundation of science lies in discovering universal necessary causal laws. There is no so-called will or spiritual effect for all natural phenomena. In the eyes of scientists, they only recognize that matter undergoes various changes under the control of natural laws. Therefore, materialistic thought is indeed very close to natural science, but materialism also regards "spirit" as a "reality" of matter. Its proposition is a metaphysical theory, which is different from experiential natural science. For example, future biology may be able to explore the relationship between biological and spiritual effects and seek the necessary laws between them, but the purpose of natural science is only to clarify the facts, and it will never subordinate spiritual effects to matter. This is just like physics studying the relationship between matter and energy. Its purpose is only to understand the facts related to the various states of matter and energy, and it does not consider subordinating "energy" to matter. At the same time, we should pay attention to the fact that natural science's research on matter certainly focuses on the observation and experiment of matter itself, but also pays attention to the correctness of thinking and the completeness of argumentation. Anyone who studies science probably knows that before a certain observation and experiment, there must first be some premonitions. Although this premonition is not necessarily correct, premonition has a significant relationship with whether the research can succeed. In short, although science absolutely emphasizes matter, it is absolutely not metaphysical materialism.

From the above, it can be seen that science has given a very deep influence to simple idealism and metaphysical mechanical materialism, forcing them to change separately. The critical philosophy and intuitive philosophy in the modern philosophical world, as well as various thoughts on vitalism, have all emerged under the baptism of science.

(IV) The contribution of science to life: In our daily life, no matter what we eat, wear, live, or travel, we rely on scientific inventions. Therefore, the function of science is very broad, and the contribution of science to life is very great.

The invention of rayon synthetic dyes and the progress of textile machines have greatly reformed our clothing. The fixation of air and the large supply of artificial fertilizers have changed agriculture, and our food is also affected by advanced science. The development of cement and steel industries has changed the style of the construction industry in the past. The progress of internal combustion engines and light metals has added automobiles and airplanes to the transportation industry from trains. In this way, the problems of living and traveling are also very different from before.

The function of science is so broad that it cannot be listed one by one, but there is a fundamental problem that must be paid attention to: that is, there must first be theoretical development in science, and then various applications can be invented, and the contribution of science to us lies only in how to adapt to nature, and we can never use science to conquer nature. Let's extend this discussion.

Science either discovers things that we cannot usually feel, or invents causal relationships that are usually neglected. Its ultimate purpose is to clarify the truth of natural phenomena, and it does not ask whether the phenomenon is useful. However, in the course of studying the truth, useful things are often discovered. This discovery is an accidental and incidental discovery. In other words, science is definitely not studied for application, but accidentally encounters application problems in the course of research. For example, in the course of broadly studying the theory of electromagnetic waves, special X-rays were accidentally discovered. At that time, no attention was paid to its use. Later, it was gradually learned that X-rays had a significant relationship with human physiology. Therefore, it is becoming more and more developed, and now it has become a specialty in medical technology. For example, Professor Ostwald was the first scholar to create theoretical chemistry. He discovered that oxygen can be oxidized to form nitric acid when studying the contact effect. At that time, nitric acid was cheaper than oxygen. This invention was completely useless, but it was very valuable in theory. Who knew that later Haber invented that aerial nitrogen can be used to synthesize oxygen. Therefore, the discovery of Professor Ostwald was used to indirectly manufacture nitric acid from aerial nitrogen. Its use was greatly clarified, so that Germany, which was blockaded in the European War, did not worry about the lack of raw materials for gunpowder production. Try to find out the various scientific problems that are currently applied and examine their origins, and those similar to the above examples are almost innumerable. It can be seen that all applied sciences are produced after the theory.

People in the primitive era were often threatened by natural disasters, so they often held terrifying concepts about nature. Until modern times, mankind used science in daily life to obtain natural benefits, as if nature could be freely driven by us, and said that civilization is the result of science conquering nature. This view is really wrong, and we must examine it. Using nature is definitely not conquering nature, because natural phenomena have certain necessary laws. All the facts that arise in nature are in accordance with these laws. How can human beings interfere with nature or conquer nature? We can only study the laws of natural phenomena, thus understand their causal relationships, and be able to predict the phenomena that should arise. For example, meteorology is very precise because of the observation of temperature and air pressure in various places, so we can know in advance that there should be strong winds and rain in a certain place at a certain time, but no matter how advanced meteorology is, it can never interfere with nature and never prevent the occurrence of strong winds and rain. Also, we make machines to use nature. The principle is only to change the contact and configuration of objects, so as to make them suitable for the realization of a certain natural law. For example, all power machines turn heat energy into work under natural laws. People can never make the machine work without fuel. The function of science can only try to save fuel as much as possible, so that the potential energy contained in it can be turned into work as much as possible. As mentioned above, it can be seen that it is not human beings who conquer nature. Human beings only adapt to nature with the development of science. (End)
