Local News

Regulations on the Use of Silver in Silver Products Issued by the Ministry: Silver Industry Held an Extraordinary General Meeting Yesterday, Resolving to Jointly Petition Nationwide for Amendments, as Reduction of Pure Silver Would Inevitably Lead to Business Closure 84

After the Ministry of Finance promulgated the regulations on the management of silver usage in silver products, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and other organizations have already complied with the directives. The Silverware Guild held an extraordinary general meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday, resolving to jointly petition with the national industry to request amendments to the management regulations. Details are recorded as follows:

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Other Organizations Comply with Directives

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and others received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance stating, "To the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal Bankers Association, Municipal Money Changers Association, Inspector General of Customs, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, Central Mint, Bureau of Unified Taxes for Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, Songjiang Transport Deputy, Exchange Supervision Committee, National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and General Inspectorate of Salt Affairs: Having examined, for the purpose of standardizing the methods for exchanging legal tender and facilitating implementation, this Ministry has detailed eight articles of exchange methods, promulgated for implementation, and (requested for reference by telegram) (ordered for compliance by telegram) to be followed in accordance with the record. Now, upon examination of Article 1, Section 1 of the aforementioned methods, it is stipulated that 'silver for industrial arts or other necessary product raw materials, as permitted by the government according to the regulations on the management of silver usage in silver products,' etc. These regulations on the management of silver usage in silver products have also been formulated by the Ministry, totaling twelve articles (as seen in previous reports in this newspaper), in addition to promulgation and submission to the Executive Yuan and distribution by telegram. This telegram is to instruct compliance and further instruct subordinate organizations to comply accordingly." The Ministry of Finance has deleted. Since receiving the telegram, the Chamber of Commerce and other organizations have separately ordered subordinate organizations to comply.

Silverware Guild Petitions for Amendments

Since the Ministry of Finance promulgated the regulations on the management of silver usage in silver products, the Silverware Guild held an extraordinary general meeting at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday. Attendees included Qingfuxing, Lao Fengxiang, Yang Qinghe, Qiu Tianbao, Qingyun, etc., chaired by Fu Shengmao. He reported that Article 2 of the Ministry's regulations stipulates, "From the date of announcement of these regulations, all silver utensils and silver ornaments manufactured shall, in principle, be made of chemical silver. If pure silver must be mixed, the amount of pure silver contained shall not exceed thirty percent." However, the guild's regulations stipulate that the content of pure silver is eighty-eight percent. He specifically put it to a vote, and the assembly believed that containing no more than thirty percent pure silver would be impossible for the silverware industry to implement. This is because (1) silverware and other items in the silverware industry are all handmade, and reducing pure silver will make them too hard to manufacture; (2) reducing pure silver will make the quality not easily white and shiny, inevitably making it impossible to operate the business. A resolution was made on the spot to jointly petition with the national industry to the Ministry, requesting amendments to the management regulations. The meeting adjourned around 5:00 PM.

Cotton Yarn Exports Gradually Become Smooth: The Future of the Yarn Industry Shows a Glimmer of Optimism 85

According to the Huadong News Agency, cotton yarn factories in the city have suspended or reduced the number of operating machines by more than half this year due to expensive cotton and cheap yarn. According to information obtained by a reporter from the Huadong News Agency, since the Ministry of Finance reformed the currency system, the import prices of Indian and American cotton have become more expensive than before due to stable exchange rates. Domestic cotton, since the Cotton Industry Control Committee has vigorously promoted reforms, has improved compared to previous years, and prices have gradually become uniform. At the same time, packaging and transportation have improved since the five banks, including the Bank of Communications, Jin Cheng Bank, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and China Agricultural Bank, organized the China Agricultural Loan Group this spring, and the cooperation between production and sales has gradually improved, showing gradual results. Therefore, the goods from Lingbao, Shaanxi, are almost comparable to Indian and American cotton, and many foreign merchants purchase and transport them abroad. Japanese merchants are even more enthusiastic. More than 2,000 bales have been shipped out since the beginning of this month. The yarn produced by domestic cotton yarn factories has also been improved again and again, and various ports in Nanyang are happy to purchase it. Therefore, the future of the yarn industry shows a glimmer of optimism. If the government uses its power to provide rediscounting from the Central Bank, reducing the interest rate on debts by about four percent, then the factories that have stopped production can immediately hope to resume work.

Rice Prices in Shanghai Decline Weakly: Top-Grade Rice Reaches a Maximum Price of Eleven Yuan and Seventy-Eight Cents 86

According to the Dagong News Agency, a month ago, various places were harvesting late rice, and the busy farming season began. Although the rice in the fields had been harvested, it had not yet been milled. Therefore, river rice arrived sparsely, with only six or seven thousand piculs per day. Recently, the busy farming season has passed, and milled rice has been sold in large quantities. Therefore, rice boats from Changshu, Wuxi, Wuxian, Kunshan, Fengjing, Songjiang, Tongli, Zhangyan, and other areas have transported rice to the city, reaching more than 20,000 packages per day.

Rumors Affect Price Decline: Since unfounded rumors occurred in Shanghai, people have been panicked. Retail stores, because rice is a bulky commodity, except for having to slightly replenish their stocks to meet the needs of customers, are mostly unwilling to purchase and hoard in large quantities, especially in the Hongkou, Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong areas. Although Tianjin, Yantai, and Shantou have sold some goods, the quantity is not large, resulting in the accumulation of river rice, and market prices have been affected and declined weakly. Top-grade rice is priced at eleven yuan and seventy-eight cents, second-grade at eleven yuan and twelve cents, third-grade at ten yuan and forty-five cents, and thin rice at nine yuan and seventy-eight cents. There is still no hope for higher prices at present.

Autumn Harvest Conditions in Various Places: The famous rice-producing areas in our country are Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and others. This year, floods have affected all provinces. According to the results of the survey, the autumn harvest conditions are roughly as follows: the harvest in Jiangsu and Zhejiang is about 70%, and the harvest in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi is about 80%. However, Anhui Province has the best harvest year, with a 100% harvest.

Silk Factories Lack Raw Materials and Suspend Production: Eagerly Awaiting the Promotion of Sericulture 87

Issue More Silkworm Eggs and Cultivate Mulberry Forests: The Silk Industry Should Also Improve Technology

According to a Dagong News Agency report, silk factories in the city have recently been short of raw materials and unable to reel silk. Therefore, as many as sixteen factories have successively suspended production since last month. By the end of this month, it is feared that all factories will suspend production. A reporter met with a prominent figure in the silk industry yesterday, who stated that the export of silk from our country has always occupied an important position. In recent years, due to the global economic downturn and the dumping of Japanese silk at depreciated prices, Chinese silk has suffered a setback, and prices have plummeted. Farmers in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas have changed to other industries because there is no profit to be made. Since the summer of this year, the Japanese silkworm-producing areas have suffered floods, and production has decreased, while demand in Europe and the United States has increased. Therefore, sales have been active, and silk prices have risen, which is a major turning point for the export of Chinese silk. Most of the suspended silk factories have resumed production one after another to meet export needs. Unfortunately, because silkworm farmers raise very few silkworms, and production is not abundant, all factories feel a lack of raw materials, which is not enough to meet the reeling needs, and they have successively stopped production in recent days, which is truly heartbreaking. Therefore, the silk industry hopes that the Construction Department of Jiangsu and Zhejiang should pay attention to (1) issuing more silkworm eggs. This year, only more than 1.8 million improved seeds were issued, and at least 6 million must be issued next year to match production and sales; (2) cultivating mulberry forests. In recent years, silkworm farmers have regarded sericulture as a daunting task because they have seen silk prices plummet. They not only do not cultivate the mulberry trees they have planted but also cut them down in large quantities. As a result, silkworm food is insufficient, causing panic. At the same time, the silk industry itself should also improve technology, such as reeling machines, silk management, and shipping, which all need to be paid close attention to so that exports can be prosperous, which can be hoped for.

Sino-US Commerce: 150th Anniversary Commemoration: A Grand Banquet Will Be Held Tomorrow Evening at the American Club: Zhang Gongquan and Others Appointed as Chairmen to Invite People from All Walks of Life to Participate 88

Tomorrow (19th) is the 150th anniversary of Sino-US commerce. The Sino-US commercial community in Shanghai, as well as the Sino-US Trade Association, the American Chamber of Commerce, and other organizations, are enthusiastically preparing to celebrate. A grand banquet will be held at 7:00 PM on this evening at the American Club on Fuzhou Road. Zhang Gongquan, President of the Sino-US Trade Association, and Luland Clinck, President of the American Chamber of Commerce, have been appointed as chairmen to express their opinions on Sino-US trade. Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance, Wu Tiecheng, Mayor, Johnson, US Ambassador, and celebrities from the Sino-US industrial and commercial sectors will all participate in the grand event. At the same time, Shi Zhaoji, our country's ambassador to the United States, and Hull, US Secretary of State, will also give speeches in Washington on this day about the history and future hopes of Sino-US commerce. It is noted that Guangzhou and New York were the earliest ports of commerce between China and the United States 150 years ago. The first American merchant ship, the "Empress of China," sailed back to New York from Guangzhou on this day. Therefore, November 19th is the Sino-US Commerce Commemoration Day. The governments and people of China and the United States hold extremely enthusiastic celebrations every year.

Keenahan Approved for Retirement: Scheduled to Leave Shanghai and Return Home: The Consul in Shanghai Is Temporarily Represented by Davis 94

According to the Continental News, Keenahan, the US Consul General in Shanghai, received a message from Washington yesterday (16th) and stated that he will leave Shanghai and return home on December 21. The news that Keenahan would retire came out in June of this year, and it will become a reality at the end of the year. However, Keenahan will stop working at the end of this month. He will spend his time in Shanghai in the third week of December on leave, and prepare everything. It is said that Mr. Davis of the US Consulate General will temporarily act as Consul General until Keenahan's successor is appointed. Shanghai has not yet received news of who Keenahan's successor will be. Davis's term of office will last until the end of the year. The new Consul General should be able to take office before the end of the year. It is rumored that Davis has a good chance of succeeding Keenahan. Keenahan has served in the consulate for 37 years. He has served as Consul General in Shanghai since 1919. The United States established a consulate in Shanghai 90 years ago. The previous 32 people who held Keenahan's position could not match Keenahan's term. Keenahan is two years past the age of retirement. Now that he is about to retire, the leader of the Shanghai consuls will also be replaced. During his 37 years of service, Keenahan has served in various parts of the world. From 1898 to 1901, he served as Consul in Aden. For the next five years, he served in Norway. From 1905 to 1910, he served in South Africa. Since 1910, he has been transferred to the East, serving as Consul in Mumbai, Singapore, and Hankou. Later, he was promoted to Consul General in Shanghai, which has been 16 years now.

Issuance of Public Works Bonds: Distributed by the National Economic Council: Public Works Are Also Hosted and Conducted by the National Economic Council 96

According to the Dagong News Agency, the National Government issued the 24th Year of the Republic of China Flood Relief Public Works Bonds, with a fixed amount of 20 million yuan, to provide relief to the flood-stricken provinces. The regulations have been reviewed and passed by the 36th meeting of the Legislative Yuan and issued on November 1st. However, because the actual issuance procedures have not been prepared, the Ministry of Finance has printed subscription certificates first, so that formal denominations can be exchanged at the time of issuance. The public bonds are divided into three types: 10 yuan, 100 yuan, and 1,000 yuan. They are all bearer bonds with an annual interest rate of 6%, issued at 98% of the face value. According to news from the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Provincial Flood Relief, the issuance of these public bonds is under the charge of the Ministry of Finance. Emergency relief in the disaster areas of the Yangtze River and Yellow River basins has been completed, and public works are urgently needed to be carried out. This time, the central government followed the precedent of providing 20 million yuan in aid to the people, and the total amount of flood relief public works bonds issued is 20 million yuan, which is enough to be distributed according to the disaster situation. In addition to the issuance matters being reviewed and handled by the Ministry of Finance, the distribution of the amount in each province is the responsibility of the National Economic Council. All dike construction and various defense construction projects in various provinces in the Yangtze and Yellow River basins, after being inspected by the National Economic Council, are being supervised by personnel dispatched by the council. Therefore, there is no fundamental problem in the issuance of these public bonds after the council has prepared and decided on the detailed distribution rules. Each province can verify and receive the bonds, mortgage them to the banking industry, and the council will still host the public works matters.

Sharp Reduction in Leather Exports This Year 100

A Total of More Than 14 Million in Six Months: A Decrease of More Than 8 Million Compared to the Same Period Last Year

According to the Dagong News Agency, leather is a special product of the northwest of our country, and the number of exports is quite large. In recent years, due to the fact that livestock breeders have adhered to the old methods and have not improved them, they have gradually declined. According to the International Trade Bureau, the total export value in the past six months of this year was more than 14.494 million yuan, a decrease of more than 8.4 million yuan compared to the same period last year. Among them, except for an increase of more than 728,000 yuan in leather blankets and rugs, other goods, such as raw buffalo hides, decreased by more than 250,000 yuan, raw cattle hides decreased by 47%, and un tanned lambskins decreased by 43%. In terms of leather sales, Hong Kong and Germany are the largest markets for raw buffalo hides, and France is the lowest. Japan is the largest market for raw cattle hides, accounting for more than 776,000 yuan, and the United States is the smallest. The United States is the largest market for dog skins and un tanned skins, accounting for more than 3.4 million yuan. Lambskins, yellow wolf skins, and leather blankets and rugs are also mainly sold to the United States, accounting for more than 6.74 million yuan.

South District Rent Reduction Committee Sends Representatives to Petition the Fifth Plenary Session 101

The Shanghai Nanshi District Rent Reduction Committee recently dispatched Shen Xinfu and others to submit a petition to the Fifth National Congress to reduce rents. The City-Wide Rent Reduction Representatives Conference resolved that, pending the promulgation of explicit rent reduction measures, in order to alleviate the city's conditions and maintain the status quo, rent for new buildings would be paid at 60% of the original rate, and rent for old buildings would revert to the original rate six years prior. If any rent reduction leads to dismissal by landlords, or if rent arrears are pursued, reports should be made immediately to the legal team of the South District Rent Reduction Committee at No. 9 Mu Di, Luxiangyuan Road, Zhian Lane. The committee will provide legal assistance. Since the beginning of this year, Shanghai courts have issued many judgments regarding lease cases, deciding on rent reductions of 70%, 80%, 90%, etc. Merchants who wish to reduce rent but are unclear about the details may directly inquire with the committee. The original text of the committee's submission to the Fifth National Congress is recorded below, petitioning for high rents in Shanghai to be reduced and requesting that the matter be submitted to the congress for deliberation and resolution, and that the National Government be requested by letter to order the Shanghai Municipal Government, local courts, and all relevant agencies to assist the affiliated associations in strictly implementing rent reduction to save people's lives, for the following reasons: It is estimated that Shanghai has a population of 3.5 million. Excluding landowners, property owners, and foreigners, numbering approximately 500,000, the remaining 3 million people must rent houses to live in. The annual rent paid, on average, accounts for approximately two-thirds of their total annual income. In the past, when the market was prosperous and commerce flourished, they could barely manage to support themselves, but now, in the midst of the global economic panic and the surging tide of domestic rural bankruptcy, Shanghai is inevitably affected. If this situation continues, not only will commerce have no way to flourish and the market will be difficult to prosper, but this huge population will also starve to death and have no way to survive. This is the first reason why rent reduction should be strictly implemented. Since the January 28th Incident, Shanghai's vitality has been severely damaged and has not yet recovered, leading to an increasing number of unemployed people and starving beggars lining the streets. People have no time to save themselves from death, let alone any purchasing power. This is why goods are piling up, sales are difficult, and financial stagnation is a concern. Various tragic phenomena are unfolding before our eyes. The reasons for this are indeed complex, but the biggest one is that rents are too high. The blood and sweat of most citizens, in addition to a large portion being used to pay rent, is insufficient to provide them with adequate food and clothing. This is the second reason why rent reduction should be strictly implemented. Since its establishment in January of last year, the committee has been actively working day and night. Now in Shanghai, under the organization of the affiliated associations, the establishment of branch associations in various streets and lanes has spread the call for rent reduction throughout the city. The impact has been such that those moved to reduce rents, such as in the Minquan Road area, have reached two-thirds. However, some are stubbornly resistant, arbitrarily preventing business operations, or listening to slander and filing lawsuits, so that seeking peace is instead met with unrest, and the burden of lawsuits increases before rent is reduced. The presiding judges, in order to consider the overall situation of the city, are unwilling to push either side to extremes and repeatedly try to mediate. The affiliated associations, caught in the middle of this insistence from both sides, are running around appealing and gently mediating, becoming hoarse and exhausted. They have submitted petitions to party and government organs several times, but this matter is of great importance, and without the force of political power, it is not enough to serve as a warning. This is why we should request that the matter be submitted to the congress for deliberation and resolution, and that the administrative organs be requested by letter to provide assistance. Third reason. Measures: (1) The congress should conduct a detailed discussion, deliberate and resolve the matter, and request the National Government by letter to order the Shanghai Municipal Government, local courts, and all relevant agencies to provide assistance in various ways, so that this rent reduction movement can be deepened and universalized, in order to achieve complete success. (2) Based on the Shanghai land price standards promulgated this year by the Shanghai Land Bureau, calculate the land price, and then add the construction cost, which will be the cost of the house. In accordance with this cost, set the rent rate, which should not exceed the statutory amount, excluding the landlord's land tax and house donation (originally one cent, now too high, to be regulated separately by the court). For those with unclear construction dates, an estimate must also be made, ensuring fairness and impartiality, so that both landlord and tenant are at peace. Rent reduction movement meets the needs of the times, and on behalf of the people, it calls out. We hope that all the party and state leaders will be concerned about the people's suffering and pay attention to it, and that they will carefully deliberate and resolve the matter in the congress discussing national affairs, and implement it vigorously. Then Shanghai will be fortunate, and China will be fortunate. The matter concerns people's lives and is a matter of urgency.

Wu Dingchang and Others to Organize a Sino-Japanese Trade Association After Returning to China 107

Actively Proceeding, Aiming for Establishment Before the Fifth of Next Month; Japan-China Trade Association to be Established Simultaneously

The Chinese Economic Delegation to Japan, led by Wu Dingchang, departed from Shanghai on October 6th and has since returned to China in stages. They are preparing for the organization of the Sino-Japanese Trade Association, scheduled to be established simultaneously in Shanghai and Tokyo before December 5th. The regulations have already been drafted. The reporter of the Jingzhe Voice Agency has obtained the details, which are recorded as follows:

Preparations for the Organization: The delegation leader Wu Dingchang, delegation members Song Hanzhang, Huang Wenzhi, Chen Guangfu, Zou Minchu, Zhou Zuomin, Qian Xinzhi, Yu Zuoting, Liu Hongsheng, Zhong Bingfeng, Xu Xinliu, Tang Shoumin, Hu Yunan, Nan Jingyong, Zhu Shigang, and secretaries and experts have returned to China in stages. During the inspection in Japan, the members of the Sino-Japanese Sub-Committee (China: Zhou Zuomin, Qian Xinzhi, Yu Zuoting; Japan: Yasukawa Yunosuke, Kodama Kenji, Suzuie Naruyoshi, etc.) held a meeting to study the economic conditions of the two countries and promote trade. It was decided to establish trade associations, called the Sino-Japanese Trade Association in China and the Japan-China Trade Association in Japan. The Sino-Japanese Trade Association is now being prepared and organized by the returning delegation leader Wu Dingchang and other delegation members, together with economic industrialists. It is scheduled to be established in Shanghai before December 5th. As for the Japan-China Trade Association, it is being prepared by Kodama Kenji, manager of the Yokohama Specie Bank, and others. It is scheduled to be established in Tokyo simultaneously with the Sino-Japanese Trade Association.

Regulations of the Association: Article 1. This association is called the Sino-Japanese Trade Association in China and the Japan-China Trade Association in Japan. Article 2. The purpose of this association is to jointly study the economic conditions of the two countries and promote trade between the two countries. Article 3. Members of this association shall be those engaged in industries in both countries and those related to them. Article 4. Applicants for membership in this association must be introduced by two or more members. In Japan, they must also be approved by the Japanese Board of Directors. In China, they must be approved by the Chinese Board of Directors. Article 5. The association shall have its headquarters in Tokyo, Japan and Shanghai, China. However, with the resolution of each board of directors, branches may be established in important commercial ports in China and Japan. Article 6. The Tokyo and Shanghai headquarters shall each have no more than 25 directors, who shall be elected separately from the members. Their term of office is three years, and they may be re-elected. Article 7. Seven or fewer standing directors shall be elected from among the directors. Article 8. Each of the Tokyo and Shanghai headquarters shall have one president. The president of the Tokyo headquarters shall be elected from among the standing directors and shall be Japanese. The president of the Shanghai headquarters shall be elected from among the standing directors and shall be Chinese. Each headquarters shall have two vice presidents, one Chinese and one Japanese, elected from among the standing directors. Article 9. Each headquarters may have a number of councilors, who shall be recommended by the board of directors. Article 10. The association shall hold a general meeting of members once a year, to be held in China or Japan in rotation. The date and location of the meeting shall be agreed upon by the two boards of directors. Article 11. In the event of special events, the association may convene an extraordinary general meeting of members after consultation between the two boards of directors. Article 12. Each board of directors shall hold a regular meeting once a month, to be convened by the president. Article 13. The association may establish various specialized committees for the purpose of carrying out its affairs separately. Article 14. The expenses of the association shall be covered by membership dues and special donations. Article 15. The membership fee is 12 yuan per person per year, to be paid in one lump sum. Article 16. The budget and final accounts of the association shall be submitted to the general meeting of members for approval by the two boards of directors. Article 17. The articles of association of the branches of the association and various detailed rules shall be negotiated and formulated by the two boards of directors. Article 18. These articles of association shall be implemented after being resolved by the general meeting of members. If it is necessary to amend them, the two boards of directors shall submit them to the general meeting of members for deliberation and revision. Addenda: Article 19. The first general meeting of members shall be held on behalf of the promoters' meeting. Article 20. The first directors shall be elected from among the promoters.

Jisheng Association's Tianmen Relief Report 110

The Chinese Jisheng Association, considering the severity of the Tianmen flood, cooperated with the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association on September 19th and publicly elected Hou Yongde as the director to go with relief workers to handle emergency relief. A total of 12,000 silver dollars were remitted before and after, and Mr. Hou Yongde and others raised 2,750 silver dollars themselves, totaling 14,750 silver dollars. Rice and beans were purchased locally and distributed to 18 districts. District 5, due to transportation difficulties, was changed to cash distribution. The association recently received a report from Mr. Hou Yongde stating that the Tianmen relief work has been completed and is now being concluded. A total of 17,663 relief tickets were collected in the 1583 districts, accounting for 61,190 large mouths and 25,242 small mouths. 446 shi, 7 dou, and 6 sheng of relief rice and broad beans were distributed, and 8,134.3 silver dollars were distributed. The purchase of rice and broad beans cost 5,538.83 silver dollars. Temporary small relief, coffin expenses, freight, remittance fees, miscellaneous expenses, etc., cost 857.377 silver dollars. The construction of the Yuxin River stone bridge cost 200 silver dollars. The total cost was 14,730.507 silver dollars, leaving a surplus of 19.493 silver dollars for disposal. The relief tickets have been handed over to the Tianmen County Government for receipt. The distribution was supervised by Commissioner Shi and the County Government to show seriousness. However, winter is approaching, and the victims who have no clothes and no food are still sleeping in the open air, exposed to the wind. The conference is sympathetic to the severity of the flood disaster and has issued humanitarian relief, but the supply is far less than the demand, and it is difficult to provide thorough relief. It is hoped that continuous assistance will be provided to save the survivors, etc. After receiving the report, the association considered that Shanghai's economy is depressed and donations are dwindling. This Tianmen relief effort was indeed a difficult undertaking, but it was only a drop in the bucket, barely enough to make a difference.

Public Security Bureau and Anti-Smoking Association to Hold Anti-Smoking Publicity Campaign Starting Today; Totaling Ten Days, Ending on the 27th; And Detaining Smokers Who Have Failed to Register 115

The Municipal Public Security Bureau, considering that since the implementation of the mandatory registration of smokers in this city, some smokers have still not surrendered themselves for registration, mostly due to misunderstanding of the laws or attempts to evade them, and have been hiding, has decided to take effective measures to promote attention among unregistered smokers, focusing on publicity and supplemented by investigation. The Seven Counties of Shangsong and Others Establish Winter Joint Defense Measures 116

The county governments of Shanghai, Songjiang, Fengxian, Nanhui, Jinshan, Qingpu, and Chuansha have, considering that their jurisdictions are traversed east-west by the Huangpu River and north-south by the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, as well as the Shanghai-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Songjiang, and Shanghai-Nanhui highways, making them strategically important hubs of transportation, and noting the severe decline in all industries, market stagnation, crop failures, rural bankruptcy, and social hardship this year, which has increased security concerns, decided to take preventative measures without delay. To maintain local stability and strengthen security, they will jointly organize a joint defense conference with Shanghai's military and police agencies during this winter period, aiming to prevent problems before they arise. The proposed joint defense measures are as follows: (1) Matters to be addressed by the joint defense will be discussed and decided by the joint defense conference. (2) The joint defense conference will be composed of the following members: (A) The county heads of each county. (B) The district chief of the First District of the Provincial Public Security Water Police. (C) The directors or section chiefs of the public security bureaus of each county. (D) The deputy battalion commanders and company commanders of the security forces stationed in each county. (E) Representatives of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. (F) Representatives of the Shanghai Municipal Security Office. (G) The director of the Shanghai Municipal Security Corps. (3) The joint defense conference will be held once a month, with the highest-ranking military, police, and political official at the meeting location serving as the chairman. Special meetings may be convened when necessary. (4) Matters decided by the joint defense conference will be handled by a joint defense office jointly formed by the military, police, and political officials of the municipality and counties. (5) The organization and detailed rules of procedure for the joint defense office will be determined at the first joint defense conference. (6) If there are any matters not covered by these measures, they may be submitted to the joint defense conference for discussion and amendment at any time, and reported to the provincial government for record. (7) These measures will be implemented upon approval by the provincial government.

Raw Silk Prices Soar - Silk and Satin Industries Increase Prices - New System to be Followed from Today 118

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association and the Electrical Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association have issued a notice regarding the soaring raw material prices and increased production costs, leading to adjustments in sales prices. The notice states: "Recently, the price of raw silk has been soaring. Factory silk has risen from over 300 yuan per dan to over 900 yuan, native silk has risen from over 10 yuan per hundred liang to over 30 yuan, and rayon has risen from 280 yuan per case to over 400 yuan. This has caused the cost of making silk to increase more than twofold. If we maintain the original selling prices, the losses would be substantial. However, in consideration of the social economy and to accommodate general consumption, we do not want to drastically increase prices. Therefore, after repeated discussions at the general meetings of member representatives, we have decided, considering all aspects, that the selling price of each item should be appropriately increased. Furthermore, because there are so many varieties of silk goods, each factory and store should separately negotiate and set new prices, print price lists, and submit them to our association for submission to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for record. The price of silk goods is calculated by the municipal foot and municipal catty. This was approved at the meeting. Since there are too many patterns of silk and crepe goods to list, in addition to each factory and store printing and delivering their own price lists, we are issuing this special notice that from today onwards, all kinds of silk and crepe goods will be adjusted in price. It is essential that we support each other and strive for survival. As for the promotion of the new system of weights and measures, the government has issued repeated orders, and our association has also repeatedly notified all our colleagues to comply. However, we are concerned that some colleagues may be unaware of the government's decrees and still use the old system of feet and catties. If this is discovered by the competent authorities or reported, resulting in penalties, it would be their own fault. Our association cannot guarantee them. We hereby solemnly declare this again, hoping that they will not wait and see and cause trouble for themselves."

Expressing Opinions to the Public Works Department Regarding Wheel Modifications - The Load of Rickshaws Should Be Changed to 1,000 Pounds for Two People

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Rikshaw Industry Mutual Aid Association has seen an increasing number of members, and its affairs have been developing quite well. At the same time, the literacy school sponsored by the association also held its opening ceremony yesterday at the Siwen Elementary School on Datong Road, Xinzha Road. Details are as follows:

Important Resolutions

Yesterday, the association discussed the recent regulations of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession regarding rickshaws. After discussion, the following opinions were expressed: (1) A letter should be sent to the Public Works Department requesting that the regulation to modify the wheels to 3.5-inch corner be changed to 3.2-inch corners for rickshaws and 2.2-inch corners for rickshaws to facilitate transportation. (2) Regarding the load-bearing issue of rickshaws, the Public Works Department should be requested to handle it in accordance with the regulations at the beginning of business in 1925: 500 pounds for a single person and 1,000 pounds for two people, in order to maintain livelihoods. (3) A letter should be sent to the Public Works Department to effectively stop the subordinate police from arbitrarily detaining rickshaws in order to ensure business. (4) It was decided that the membership registration for the association would be extended to the end of December.

Tan Huizhu Sentenced to Imprisonment for Abuse of Maid - Sentenced to One Year and Six Months of Imprisonment 121

Miss Tan Huizhu from Guangdong, who lives at 47 Deren Lane, Xingjia Wood Bridge, Zhabei, was recently reported to the local court for abusing her eight-year-old maid, An Xuejuan, by neighbors who felt sorry for her. Prosecutor Tang summoned the case for investigation and found it to be true. After examining Xuejuan's injuries, a public prosecution was filed according to the law. Tan Huizhu was released on bail of 1,000 yuan to await instructions. A public trial was held by Judge Zhang Shao a few days ago. Tan Huizhu strongly denied the abuse and injury, and claimed that Xuejuan was her cousin. As for the scars on her cheeks, she said that they were caused by sores that itched and she scratched them herself. When Xuejuan was questioned, she said, "I am eight years old. Huizhu is my cousin. The scars on my face were scratched by myself. Huizhu treats me very kindly on weekdays." After hearing the testimony of witness Wang Qiming, the judge believed that the case was clear and concluded the trial. The court opened the case in the afternoon and announced the verdict. Tan Huizhu was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for inflicting abuse on a girl under the age of sixteen and hindering the natural development of her body, in order to serve as a warning. Tan Huizhu refused to accept the sentence and will file an appeal according to the law.

Bicycle Knocked Down by Car - Xu Chunsong Dies Tragically 122

The deceased's father sues the driver - the court is discussing the case and will investigate further before the next trial

Xu Chunsong, 38 years old, a copper craftsman residing at 104 Shuinong, Xiaoshadu, West Shanghai, was riding his bicycle on business on the afternoon of the 14th of last month. At 2:30 PM, he was traveling from east to west on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. When he reached number 704, a truck number Fa Er San Er Er, driven by Zhou Hequan (32 years old, resident of 8 Rongshou Lane, Xiamen Road), a Wuxi native employed by the French Public Works Department, was heading to the Tailasituo Road Small Hospital to pick up Chinese police officers who had been vaccinated at the Avenue Joffre Police Station, also traveling from east to west in the same direction as Xu. Xu did not give way to the truck, and was hit by the truck's rear fender. He was injured and immediately taken to Guangci Hospital by Zhou. Zhou reported the incident to the police station. Xu died that evening due to his injuries. The body was taken to the coroner's office. The case was reported to the prosecutor of the Second Special Court, who confirmed the death. The body was placed in a coffin by relatives. The situation was reported in this newspaper. Later, the French Police Department measured and inspected the scene of the accident and concluded that the defendant Zhou Hequan was driving properly and that the accident was caused by the deceased's carelessness. Therefore, no public prosecution was filed against the defendant. The deceased's father, Xu Daming, 58 years old, disagreed with the police department's decision and filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, suing Zhou Hequan for causing death by negligence. He requested a trial and compensation for damages. The court accepted the complaint and Judge Li Changnian of the Criminal Court summoned both parties for questioning on the afternoon of the previous day. Both parties arrived on time. The plaintiff first stated that his son had been killed in a car accident and knelt on the ground to beg for justice. The defendant Zhou Hequan stated that he was driving in accordance with the regulations and that the deceased did not give way, became frightened, and fell behind his car. Kang Si Dading Mi Heyi Liufu (transliteration), a person registered with the French Police Department, testified about witnessing the accident. The court ordered an investigation and rescheduled the trial for the 21st.

Divorce Case Concluded - Another Lawsuit to Confirm Parentage 123

Lu Zhubao sues Xu Shenhai - mediation fails and formal litigation begins

Xu Shenhai, a local resident residing at 140 Liujiazhai, Jules Plaisant Road, French Concession, is a foreman in a certain machinery factory, with a wealthy life. He married Lu Zhubao, a woman from Ningbo, through a matchmaker. After they married, their relationship was very close. In the spring of last year, the couple suddenly had a quarrel, and Lu left without saying goodbye. After a long time without returning, Xu published a notice in the newspaper warning Lu. At that time, Lu's parents also published a notice in the newspaper stating that they had severed their relationship with their daughter. Lu then filed a lawsuit with the court, requesting a divorce from Xu. The litigation lasted for years, but it was still not resolved. It was not until the 3rd of this month that both parties reached an agreement, with the mediation of friends and the lawyers of both parties proving and establishing a divorce agreement. Xu paid Lu 600 yuan for alimony, and both parties officially signed the agreement and separated. The next day, Lu Zhubao filed another lawsuit with the Civil Court of the Second Special Court, requesting mediation to confirm Xu Shenhai's biological son. According to the claim, the petitioner was two months pregnant when she left home last year. On the 19th day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar, she gave birth to a son named Huifang. She had asked someone to notify Xu Shenhai of this. Xu Shenhai had been involved in litigation for a long time and was struggling financially. Therefore, he signed the divorce agreement, which stated that the child born by Xu and Lu was not Xu Shenhai's son. He was unable to agree to sign the agreement at the time, but he was forced to do so due to financial hardship. If he did not sign, the mother and son would be separated and would inevitably die together. After considering it again and again, he had no choice but to sign the agreement. After receiving the alimony, she would seek a fair judgment from the law. She did not want to starve to death, and Huifang did not want to be a fatherless child. According to the law, the relationship between father and son cannot be severed. Therefore, she is acting as the agent of Xu Huifang to file a lawsuit against Xu Shenhai to confirm parentage, requesting that the case be summoned for mediation, etc. The court accepted the complaint and Judge Wu Xiaoke specially opened the Civil Court Seven on the previous day to summon both parties for mediation. The petitioner Xu Zhuanfang was brought to the court by her legal guardian, her mother Lu Zhubao, and testified about the previous events. The opposing party, Xu Shenhai, was represented by his lawyer and expressed his objection. The court then announced that the mediation had failed and ordered the petitioner to file a formal lawsuit before adjourning the court.

Telephone Call-Based Charging - French Municipal Council Waiting for Decision - But According to French Experts, Implementation Should Be Without Difficulty 124

Regarding the Shanghai Telephone Company's request to implement a call-based charging system and increase telephone fees, after the Public Works Department of the Public Concession hired telephone experts from China, Britain, the United States, and Japan to form a special committee to jointly study the report, the committee's recommendations have been accepted by the Bureau's Public Utilities Committee and the directors. After the special committee concluded, the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department immediately began negotiations with the relevant authorities of the Shanghai Telephone Company for implementation. In addition, the experts also gave additional advice on the widespread use of technical talents and the reduction of salaries for senior internal staff. They also agreed to consider improvement. However, everything still needs to be reported to the British head office before a decision can be made. At the same time, the Public Works Department has forwarded the report to the French Concession Municipal Council for reference and to solicit opinions. The French authorities are currently considering whether to implement the new system consistently with the Public Concession on March 1st of next year. However, Mr. Lei, an American expert stationed in Shanghai, visited the French authorities and French telephone experts after returning to Shanghai from Beijing, explaining the recommendations of the report in his personal capacity. According to the opinions of French experts, the new system should have no difficulties in future implementation within the French Concession.

The Zhabei Charity Group Petitions the Municipal Government to Implement Baojia System Quickly 128

The Zhabei Charity Group, in view of the fact that this city is the largest commercial port in the Far East, with a dense population and uneven quality, and that the number of unemployed vagrants is not small, and that incidents of kidnapping and robbery are often heard, the group specially petitioned the municipal government to quickly implement the Baojia system. The original presentation is recorded as follows: "It is requested to quickly implement the Baojia system to ban vagrants and maintain the business city. It is found that Shanghai is a mixed place with a large population. According to the latest survey, the population is about one million. Among them, the quality is uneven, and the number of unemployed vagrants is not small. To put it bluntly, kidnapping and robbery, to put it mildly, blackmail and theft, happen every day. Charitable merchants regard these people as snakes and scorpions. In addition, the floods in various provinces have caused disasters, and there are countless refugees who have fled to Shanghai to make a living. If this continues, a good business place may have uneasy phenomena. In the blink of an eye, the winter defense will be coming. Although there are military and police protection, it is inevitable that the villains will hide. If you want to eliminate bandits, there is nothing better than the Baojia system. The central government has long had a clear statement, and it is not far from holding it. The provinces and counties have already achieved success. This city is the largest commercial port in the Far East, with a dense population. Since the household registration has been cleared, it can still be implemented quickly. For this reason, I would like to ask your government to quickly implement the Baojia system, and all unemployed and bad elements will be strictly banned, so that Shanghai's security can be cleared without worry."

County People's Education Center Regularly Holds Plowing Cattle Competition 133

Cai Wuji is hired as chief judge at the center on the 24th of this month.

The seventh plowing cattle competition of the Zhuanqiao People's Education Center in the county was decided at the 363rd center affairs meeting to be held on the 24th of this month (Sunday). Letters have already been sent to all sectors to solicit prizes, and Cai Wuji, Wang Zhaoji, Cheng Shaozhou, Chen Shungeng, Wu Huanru, Wu Deming, Wu Gengrong, Shen Baixian, Zhao Wu, Shen Jiucheng, Pan Weiyuan, Yang Huiming, He Ruibao, Zhao Songlin, Tang Yincheng, Zhang Lianqing, Yu Quansheng, Liu Yaoshan, Gu Tuxiang, Yan Qiugeng, and others have been hired as judges, with Cai Wuji as the chief judge. A preparatory committee has also been established, with Director Zhang serving as a member, and Cai Wuji, Wu Deming, Shen Jiucheng, Sun Zhongji, Jin Linrong, and Ru Bocai have also been hired. The methods are as follows:

Competition Methods: (1) Purpose: To promote the health of plowing cattle and increase work efficiency. (2) Date: November 24th (the 29th day of the tenth lunar month) from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM. (3) Venue: Zhuanqiao Daidan Field on Hu-Min Road. (4) Members: Anyone raising plowing cattle within the center's area of responsibility can participate in the competition as a member of this association. (5) Participation Procedures: Members must bring their cattle to the venue, register at the registration desk, receive a competition number, and hang the number plate on the cattle. The cattle must then be entrusted to the designated location for judging by the judges. Cattle cannot be freely taken out of the venue until the end of the competition. (6) Classification: Participating cattle will be divided into yellow cattle, water buffalo, and other bulls, and then grouped according to age. (7) Judging: This association will hire ten experts and ten experienced farmers as judges. This year's judging will be divided into two categories: physique and strength. (8) Lecture: At 3:00 PM, there will be a lecture on common knowledge of cattle feeding. (9) Treatment: Participating cattle found to have ailments will be treated by a veterinarian. (10) Gifts: Each participating member will receive a piece of agricultural equipment (upon presentation of a voucher) and a rough meal (upon presentation of a voucher). (11) Awards: The owners of outstanding plowing cattle in each group will be given prizes by this association as an encouragement. (12) Supplementary Rules: Members of this association are welcome to join the Livestock Improvement Promotion Association.

Review standards: divided into overview, head and neck, forequarters, midsection, and hindquarters. Overview accounts for fifteen points, divided into weight, physique, action, temperament, and condition. Head and neck account for ten points, divided into head, forehead, eyes, ears, horns, and jaw neck. Forequarters account for twenty-five points, divided into shoulder, elbow, forearm, knee, and meridian. Midsection accounts for ten points, divided into hock, hoof, chest ribs, back, and abdomen. Hindquarters account for thirty points, divided into loin corners, hips, clavicle, thigh, groin, hind legs, ankle, tibia, hock, ball range, and hoof.

The Nanjing Road Rent Reduction Issue Urgently Awaits Resolution - The Hardoon Company and Tenants Sue Each Other in Court 134

In recent years, China's rural areas have been bankrupted, disasters have been frequent, the social economy has been exhausted, people's purchasing power has been weak, and commercial goods have been stagnant. Commerce has been declining day by day. In the early days of currency reform, follow-up measures were not yet in place. Various commodity prices, directly and indirectly, have been rising. As the price of gold rises, the cost of purchasing industrial raw materials from abroad increases, making it more difficult to sell products. Businesses will become increasingly difficult. Although Nanjing Road is known as the bustling commercial district in Shanghai, more than twenty businesses have closed down this year. Although some new businesses have opened, there are still many vacant houses. This situation is rare in decades. In addition, the rent for commercial housing on Nanjing Road is expensive. In prosperous times, the burden is indirectly passed on to consumers, and the stores themselves do not feel the pain. They are often willing to pay large amounts of rent and "digging fees," even tolerating unfair contracts that unilaterally benefit the owners, gradually cultivating the insatiable desires of owners and managers. In the spring of this year, most stores on Nanjing Road suffered from high rents and urgently sought relief by petitioning various owners to reduce rents. Except for the Hardoon Company, which consistently refused, almost all cases were resolved. It is now heard that the company and tenants have already filed lawsuits in court over the rent reduction issue. The tenants have collected evidence that other owners have indeed reduced rents and are prepared to present it to the judge at the trial, requesting that the judge, while not violating legal principles, take into account the actual commercial situation and make a fair judgment.

Court Entrusts Land Valuation, Requests the Land Bureau to Complete It Within a Time Limit, Lawyers Association Sent a Letter to the Land Bureau Yesterday 136

The Shanghai Bar Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau yesterday, stating: "According to a proposal from a member, when land in this city is involved in debt lawsuits and is ordered by the court to be auctioned, the court often commissions the Municipal Land Bureau to assess the price as a standard for execution of the auction. However, the Municipal Land Bureau's valuation often takes four or five months or even a year to complete, which is far slower than the rapid valuation of the current Concession's Bureau of Public Works, causing complaints from the parties to the lawsuit. It is proposed that a letter be sent to the Municipal Land Bureau, requesting that it promptly order that valuations entrusted in the future be completed within two weeks to facilitate execution, etc. This matter has been submitted to the joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committee for discussion and resolution. Accordingly, we are writing to your bureau to investigate and handle the matter. If the court commissions the valuation of land prices in the future, it is hoped that you will order the matter to be completed within two weeks to facilitate convenience."

According to the Japanese-language "Mainichi Shimbun," a recent survey found that there are a total of 102 Japanese-run food and beverage establishments, including 43 restaurants, 40 cafes, and 18 navy-designated cafeterias, a decrease of 15 from last year. In terms of origin, those from Nagasaki and Kyushu account for the majority, followed by people from Kumamoto, Fukuoka, and Oita prefectures. Recently, the yen has risen again, and the Lunar New Year is approaching, so development is expected. However, in the past half month, due to the spread of rumors of spirits, customers have been reluctant to come.

Hu Xiyuan Writes to the Federation of Trade Unions to Advise Raw Material Merchants Not to Raise Prices Too Sharply 140

Hu Xiyuan, a member of the All-China Federation of Industry and Commerce and General Manager of the Yapu Er Factory, in view of the recent sharp rise in raw materials, which has greatly affected the cost of industrial products, wrote to the Federation requesting that it find a way to advise raw material merchants not to raise prices too sharply, causing harm to all parties. The letter stated (excerpt): "Since the implementation of the legal tender, the bargaining chips have been active, and there is hope for practical relief in rural areas. The purchasing power of the interior can gradually increase, and the prices of various commodities, on the water level line, can be reasonably raised according to their own needs. Industry and commerce can gradually enter a prosperous state as a result, which is what we extremely hope for. However, in recent observations of the conditions of various industries, in this turbulent period of legal tender implementation, there is an uneven distribution of joy and sorrow. The reason for this is that the price of raw materials has risen too sharply. For example, the price of cloth has not risen as much as the price of cotton, and the price of silk has soared, but the selling price of silk products has not been fully raised. However, this may be blamed on the trend of the international trade environment, which cannot be stopped. As for the majority of miscellaneous materials needed by light industry, according to surveys, most of them have not been affected in any way. However, raw material merchants have been psychologically affected by the currency system reform and have suddenly raised prices. This is indeed numerous. Small and medium-sized factories with insufficient inventory, on the one hand, cannot increase the selling price because purchasing power has not yet increased sharply, and on the other hand, purchase high-priced raw materials, which suddenly increases costs. In this contradictory environment, we feel deep pain. As a result, the products of the manufacturing plant are wandering on divergent paths, and the transactions of raw material merchants are also hesitant to wait and see. This creates a sluggish sales situation for goods in all aspects. This kind of self-inflicted and self-created business policy should first prompt the raw material merchants to realize the need to seek mutual benefits. This association is a large group of national industries and should request that raw material merchants in various places be advised not to seek too rapid a rise in the price of various raw materials, so as to reduce their own business and increase the costs of manufacturing plants. (The following is omitted.)"

Incoming Letters

The Path to Political System Reform (Continued) 155

— Pan Gongzhan

(Shanghai, November of the 24th Year)

——Respectfully dedicated to all comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Kuomintang and gentlemen who are fond of discussing political system reform—

However, while the spirit of political tutelage should be thoroughly implemented, drafting the constitution should not be delayed. Why? Because drafting a constitution is one thing, and implementing it is another. Drafting it early is beneficial for propaganda and research; delaying implementation is beneficial for careful consideration that aligns with the national conditions. The 22nd article of the Founding Program clearly stipulates: "The draft constitution should be based on the Founding Program and the achievements of the 'political tutelage' and 'constitutional governance' periods, discussed and drafted by the Legislative Yuan, and disseminated to the public for adoption and implementation when the time is right." This shows that drafting is the first step, propaganda is the second step, adoption is the third step, and implementation is the fourth and final step. What is particularly important to note is that drafting the constitution should occur after the "political tutelage" period and the "beginning of constitutional governance." Therefore, striving for effective political tutelage to enable local people to govern themselves, paving the way for the "beginning of constitutional governance," and drafting a constitution based on the experiences of both periods are not contradictory. Some people believe that the constitution conflicts with political tutelage, while others believe that the constitution must be promulgated and implemented immediately after drafting. These are all narrow-minded and rigid views.

The failures of the political stage in recent years lie in the abundance of institutions with unclear systems and the multitude of committee members without assuming responsibility. As a result, despite the overlapping government offices and the overflowing number of personnel, there has been no improvement in political progress or reduction in national difficulties. Therefore, if we draft a constitution that embodies the spirit of political tutelage, we must first ensure that the political institutions (i.e., government organizations) prescribed in the constitution are tightly organized and flexible, with clear systems and specific responsibilities. The government should truly exercise "governing power," ensuring that those responsible for administrative responsibilities have ample opportunity to develop their talents, strengthen their authority, and avoid excessive constraints. At the same time, in the process of implementing policies, the government must be guided and supervised by the Kuomintang, which is building the nation based on the Three Principles of the People, ensuring that national policy decisions do not deviate from the Three Principles of the People. Only in this way will the national revolution not be in vain, and only in this way will political system reform not stray into erroneous paths.

When the constitution is first promulgated and the preparations for constitutional governance begin, the Kuomintang must still represent the people and bear the significant responsibility of guiding and supervising the government. In other words, during this period, which we can tentatively call the "party and people co-governance period" as a transition stage from "party rule" to "people's rule," the Kuomintang is still representing the people and exercising a portion of the "political power" in reality. Since the Kuomintang's responsibilities cannot be easily dismissed, it should first examine the shortcomings in its organization over the past few years and attempt to "revitalize itself." First, the party in the past did not train its members like soldiers, leading to loose organization and lax discipline. Second, the party in the past did not implement its political program like a creed, leading to broken promises and loss of trust with the people. Third, the party in the past did not concentrate its power under one leader, leading to factions, suspicions, and exploitation by those who sow discord. Fourth, the party in the past did not make every effort to eradicate corruption, leaving the vast bureaucracy shrouded in dark miasma, blurring the people's understanding of revolutionary work. In short, the Kuomintang is ultimately the most historic and powerful party. As long as it internally reforms its organization, strengthens it, and eliminates past malpractices, it can naturally take on the responsibility of guiding and supervising the government. Kuomintang members should have this confidence: as long as members are aware, work hard, and organize tightly, they can not only build the nation but also govern it well.

Having briefly explained the path to political system reform that I have considered, I will now write out the main outline of the constitution draft that I hope for and the important points for revising the Kuomintang's general regulations on the left. I welcome experts to provide guidance! (To be continued)

A Visit to a Cannery 156

— Jin Huating

——Taikang Cannery——

Since China opened its doors to the world, foreign goods have flooded the market due to our inability to fully control tariffs. The outflow of cash over the years has been difficult to calculate. Even for common canned foods, biscuits, and candies, the annual imports are enormous. Fortunately, Chinese merchants have gradually become aware of this over the past twenty years, and they have established canneries one after another, imitating and researching diligently, which has enabled them to compete with foreign merchants and recover a considerable amount of lost profits. In order to understand the actual situation of the manufacture of canned foods, biscuits, candies, etc., this newspaper visited the "Taikang Cannery," which has a larger scale and more complete equipment, for a tour. The observations are recorded below for reference by those engaged in this industry.

The Establishment History of Taikang: The Taikang Company was founded in Jinan in the third year of the Republic of China (1914) by Mr. Le Rucheng, Mr. Xu Yongrui, and Mr. Zhuang Shikang with a capital of 10,000 yuan. It was initially an unlimited partnership that specialized in selling various Chinese and foreign foods. Later, to resist foreign goods, they imitated and manufactured their own products. After several years of research, they finally succeeded. By the seventh year of the Republic of China (1918), their products had spread throughout Shandong and the cities of Beijing and Tianjin. Wholesale business expanded from Shanghai to Hankou and other places. In the tenth year of the Republic of China (1921), it was renamed an unlimited company and registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the Beijing government. In the same year, a wholesale office was established in Shanghai. In the twelfth year of the Republic of China (1923), in view of the seafood and bamboo shoots produced in the south, a factory was built in Shanghai's Nanshi Manufacturing Bureau Road to adapt to local conditions. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927), as the products were widely sold, but limited by assets, the supply could not meet the demand. Therefore, it was reorganized into a limited company with a paid-up capital of 150,000 yuan. The following year, it was registered with the National Registration Bureau of the National Government. Le Rucheng served as general manager. In the twenty-third year of the Republic of China (1934), the general distribution office was moved to the newly built market at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Yunnan Road, and distribution offices were added in other places successively. At this time, the company's total turnover had reached 1.1 million yuan. Its products spread throughout the country and the South Seas Islands. However, at the same time, European and American merchants also set up factories in the Shanghai concessions to avoid tariff restrictions and engage in even greater dumping. From then on, the competition between Chinese and foreign companies began to intensify. In order to ensure the survival of domestic products, the company convened a shareholders' meeting, increased its capital to 500,000 yuan, and purchased a 1933-style "Great" biscuit machine from the United Kingdom to speed up production and reduce costs. It also purchased land near Fenglin Bridge in southern Shanghai to build a new factory, striving to improve its content and equipment. The entire factory is divided into three major systems: management, engineering, and administration. The engineering system has the broadest scope, including biscuit manufacturing, machine-made cans, canned food manufacturing, candy manufacturing, Western-style pastry manufacturing, Chinese-style pastry manufacturing, bread manufacturing, preserved tangerine peel manufacturing, biscuit packaging, candy packaging, and chemical testing. In addition, worker education, hygiene, and other aspects are also well-organized, making it a modern factory.

Manufacturing Methods of Various Products: The factory produces seven types of products: (1) Chinese pastries, (2) Western pastries, (3) bread, (4) biscuits, (5) canned goods, (6) candies, and (7) preserved tangerine peels. They are widely sold, and the canned goods and biscuits are the most profitable. The manufacturing methods and ingredients of each product are roughly as follows: First, the raw materials department has a total of 1,200 kinds, divided into oil and spices. Two-thirds are domestic, and one-third are imported. Second, the Chinese pastry manufacturing department mostly relies on manual labor, using 40% eggs, 30% flour, 25% sugar, and 15% yeast to make various Chinese pastries, which are baked. Third, the Western pastry manufacturing department uses 20% butter, 20% flour, 40% eggs, and 20% sugar and yeast to make various Western pastries, which are steamed. Fourth, the bread manufacturing department first mixes flour and yeast, then ferments for six hours, and finally bakes in an oven. The working hours are from 7 pm to 2 am the next morning, and the daily output is based on the amount of orders received in the afternoon and evening. Fifth, the canned goods manufacturing and seasoning department first sends the raw materials to the manufacturing department for washing after being identified by the chemical laboratory, and then cooks and cans them separately. There are a total of 105 flavors, divided into five categories: fish, meat, game, vegetables, and fruits. Sixth, the can welding department is used to repair and weld various cans. Seventh, the equipment department is used to repair various machines. Eighth, the machine and furnace room is used to power the machines and boilers in various departments. Ninth, the machine-made can department specializes in manufacturing various cans. The iron sheets used are entirely purchased from the United Kingdom and the United States. Each box weighs 200 pounds, with 112 sheets, worth about 40 yuan in national currency. After the cans are made, they must be transferred to a vacuum machine and a water tank for disinfection before they can be used. Tenth, the biscuit manufacturing department is divided into five steps: (A) Mixing, which involves mixing 70% flour, 20% sugar, and 10% yeast with a machine. There are more than 40 kinds. High-quality biscuits use more foreign materials, accounting for about 40%, while medium and low-quality ones use less, accounting for about 15%. (B) Rolling skin, after the mixed raw materials are mixed, they are transferred to a rolling machine to roll the raw materials into thin skin, and then cleaned with a brush. (C) Printing, after the thin skin is cleaned with a brush, it is immediately passed through a printing machine to print various patterns on the biscuits and cut them into squares at the same time. (D) Baking, after being cut into squares, they are immediately sent into a 450-degree oven, entering and exiting at the same time, with a baking time of five minutes, and then the finished product is obtained. (E) Packaging, the baked biscuits are sent to the packaging department for packaging or canning. In addition, the procedures for candies and preserved plums are very simple. Candies only need to mix sugar with peanuts, melon seeds, meat, or walnuts and cut them into squares. Preserved plums only need to collect a large amount of green plums when they are on the market, pickle them with salt first, dry them after a certain period of time, and then crush them so that they can be added with various ingredients to make various preserved plums at any time.

Special Chemical Testing Laboratory: In order to ensure that various products meet hygiene regulations, the factory has established a chemical testing laboratory in the general factory, specializing in testing various raw materials and products for other unhealthy or toxic substances, especially for canned foods such as fish, meat, and game, paying extra attention.

Business Overview and Others: The factory has a capital of 500,000 yuan. The business has been good over the years. Last year, the total turnover reached as high as 2 million yuan. There are six distribution departments in Shanghai, and more than 1,300 sales agents across the country. The daily consumption of eggs is 500 pounds, and the consumption of flour is 250 bags (the output of the new factory). The entire factory has more than 230 male workers and more than 200 female workers, implementing a contract system. The monthly income of each worker is about 12 or 13 yuan. The monthly salary of technical foremen is as high as 120 yuan. The factory base covers more than 18 acres. In addition to the self-built factory buildings, offices, and halls, workers' dormitories and workers' family dormitories are also attached to accommodate the workers and their families. The rent for each apartment is only 5 yuan per month, so all male and female workers are very happy.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Inspection: Yang Zhensheng Convenes Symposium in Hubei 166

(Hankou, 16th) Yang Zhensheng, inspector of the Ministry of Education, convened a symposium with senior officials at the Department of Education at 2 PM on the 16th. Cheng Qibao and section chiefs and above attended to discuss various improvement issues.

Revised Regulations for the Review of Educational Textbooks 167

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the Education Departments and Bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 16th, stating that the Regulations for the Review of Educational Textbooks were promulgated and implemented in the 18th year. Now that several years have passed, some of the provisions of the original regulations are no longer applicable and should be amended, added, or deleted. The regulations have been revised again. In addition to the promulgation and separate orders, three copies of the revised Regulations for the Review of Educational Textbooks are enclosed for your information and to instruct your subordinates to comply with them accordingly. This order includes the issuance of five copies of the revised Regulations for the Review of Educational Textbooks.

Revised Regulations for the Review of Educational Textbooks

Article 1 Educational textbooks used in schools must be reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Education according to law. Those that have not been reviewed and issued a license, or those whose approval has expired, shall not be published, and schools shall not adopt them.

Article 2 Publishers or authors of educational textbooks shall submit two copies each of the manuscript and printed samples before publication to request review. The manuscript shall be written in regular script or typed (those who voluntarily use typesetting shall be allowed). The paper, number of pages, number of lines, number of words, as well as charts, formats, positions, horizontal and vertical writing, etc., of the original and duplicate manuscripts shall be completely the same. The printed sheets submitted together with the manuscript shall have the text on both sides and the cover, the author's name, and the price printed on them.

Article 3 Educational textbooks used in schools that contain scientific terms, foreign names, place names, and other proper nouns shall compile a table of corresponding Chinese and foreign terms (scientific terms that have been announced by the Ministry of Education shall use the announced standard) and attach it to the end of the book for reference.

Article 4 When submitting educational textbooks for review, a review fee shall be submitted along with the manuscript and sample. For educational textbooks used in elementary schools, 30 times the price of the entire book shall be submitted. For educational textbooks used in secondary schools, 20 times the price of the entire book shall be submitted. For all types of wall charts, 10 times the price of the entire chart shall be submitted.

Article 5 When submitting educational textbooks for review, the entire manuscript shall be submitted at once. Those that are incomplete or do not comply with the provisions of Articles 2, 3, and 4 shall not be reviewed.

Article 6 If the price of an educational textbook submitted for review is too high, the Ministry of Education may, at its discretion, order it to be reduced. If the price must be increased after review, the reasons shall be explained and submitted for approval.

Article 7 If the content of an educational textbook submitted for review needs to be revised, the Ministry of Education shall instruct the submitter to revise or rewrite it within six months according to the comments, and then resubmit it for review. Those who submit the revised or rewritten version after the deadline shall not be reviewed. The revised or rewritten version referred to in the preceding paragraph shall be submitted in duplicate in accordance with the provisions of Article 2.

Article 8 When submitting a revised or rewritten version and a printed version after review, the original number of volumes, pages, and lines in the previous manuscript shall be indicated in the revised section. Two copies of the printed version referred to in the preceding paragraph shall be submitted.

Article 9 The manuscript of an educational textbook may be printed only after it has been reviewed and approved. After the printed version is submitted for verification and found to be correct, the Ministry of Education shall issue a review and approval certificate.

Article 10 The Ministry of Education shall announce the following items in the Ministry of Education Gazette for educational textbooks that have been reviewed and approved: 1. Title of the book, 2. Number of volumes, 3. Price, 4. Author's name, 5. Submitter, 6. Type of school for which it is intended, 7. Date of approval, 8. License number, 9. Expiration date.

Article 11 Educational textbooks that have been reviewed and approved shall indicate the Ministry of Education's approval word on the cover of each book and shall indicate on the bottom the words "Approved by the Ministry of Education in (year) (month)" and the license number.

Article 12 If facts change or the content of an educational textbook that has been reviewed and approved is inappropriate and needs to be revised, the publisher or author shall immediately revise it and submit two copies of the revised version for review within three months. If the deadline is exceeded, the approval will be revoked.

Article 13 The validity period of the approval of educational textbooks shall be three years for secondary schools and four years each for simple normal schools and elementary schools. A re-review shall be submitted four months before the expiration date. When submitting for re-review, a review fee shall be submitted separately in accordance with the provisions of Article 4.

Article 14 If a publisher violates the provisions of Article 1 or deliberately disobeys an order prohibiting publication, he/she shall be subject to administrative sanctions or legal penalties as appropriate.

Article 15 These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation.
