High School Students Not Allowed to Transfer to Normal Schools 173

Ministry of Education Instructs Jiangsu Education Department to Notify

The Ministry of Education has strict restrictions on the acceptance of transfer students to normal schools. According to the provisions of Article 78 of the regulations, they must have a transfer certificate or transcript from another normal school with matching semesters and pass the placement examination to be qualified. The Jiangsu Education Department recently reported that each term, when recruiting transfer students, there are very few scholars from other normal schools. However, first-year high school students, either because they aspire to study normal education or because they cannot afford the expenses and receive free treatment, have requested to transfer. According to the rules, this is not in compliance. Considering that the students have potential, and that there is a shortage of teachers as compulsory education is being promoted, can we make an exception to cultivate talent? The Education Department forwarded the request to the Ministry of Education for review. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education instructed that the acceptance of transfer students to grades above the second semester of normal schools is limited to those who have the qualifications for matching semesters from similar schools. The proposal to allow high school students to transfer to normal schools for study should not be considered.

Polish Embassy Introduces Polish Education Situation 175

To provide reference for those who aspire to study in Poland.

The Polish government has specially established a scholarship for Chinese students, and the Ministry of Education held exams on the 15th and 16th of this month, as reported in various newspapers. Regarding the situation of Polish education and admission procedures, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs inquired with the Polish Embassy, which has responded with detailed information and instructed the Ministry of Education to announce it to all universities, so as to provide reference for those who aspire to study in Poland. The following is an excerpt of the Polish education situation:

Polish Education

Cracow, founded by King Kagimeijz in 1364, is a world-renowned academic institution. The astronomer Nicolas Copernicus once studied deeply there. Polish education continued to progress without interruption in the 16th and 17th centuries. Unfortunately, the progress of education was interrupted by the division of the 18th century. Poland established the Commission of National Education in 1773, which was the beginning of the European Ministry of Education. In 1918, Poland restored its country, and everything old was renewed. The government and people suffered from the pain of the Great War and the Russian-Polish War, as well as the hardship of economic chaos. However, they spared no effort in the construction of education, so the results were remarkable. Recently, there have been 22 universities.

Two Types of Secondary Schools

There are two types of secondary schools in Poland. Type A includes Latin, and Type B does not include Latin but focuses on mathematics and physics. After passing the secondary school graduation examination, students can enter any commercial, agricultural, or other university. The average age of first-year university students is about 19 years old. The Senate, an organization of professors headed by the Rector Magnificas, manages the school's academics. The language used in Polish universities is Polish, which is different from German, French, and Russian.

Five National Universities

There are five national universities with an annual budget of approximately 31 million Solys, equivalent to 16 million Chinese dollars. There are more than 680 teaching staff and more than 2,000 assistant teachers. (1) Csacow University, one of the oldest universities in Europe, has 7,000 male and female students and offers courses in law, theology, medicine, literature, and science. (2) Warasw University, founded in the 16th century, has five departments: law, theology, medicine, literature, and science. There are more than 3,000 students. (3) Lwow University, founded in the 17th century, has four departments: law, theology, medicine, literature, and science. The number of students is often more than 2,000. (4) Warasw University, founded in 1817, is the largest university with departments of law, theology, medicine, literature, pharmacology, and veterinary medicine. There are more than 10,000 students. (5) Poznan University, founded in 1920, has agricultural and forestry departments in addition to ordinary departments. There are approximately 4,000 students.

Other Specialized Schools

(1) The Warsaw Institute of Technology has seven departments: engineering, architecture, machinery, water conservancy, electrical engineering, chemistry, and surveying. There are approximately 2,000 students. (2) The Lwow Institute of Technology has six departments: engineering, architecture, mechanical chemistry, agriculture and forestry. There are approximately 2,000 students. (3) The Crawow Mining School has two departments: mining and metallurgy. It is the only school that studies this engineering field. There are approximately 600 students. (4) The Warsaw Higher Agricultural School has three departments: agriculture, forestry, and horticulture. Poland is an agricultural country, and agriculture has been extremely developed in recent years. New methods are used for cultivation. The students of this school use the summer vacation to work in the countryside for practical work, and at the same time, they can study rural agriculture, loan consumption cooperatives, local autonomy, public health, and public education. (5) The Warsaw Higher School of Commerce is a private school, but under special legislation, it enjoys the same rights as other higher schools. There are approximately 1,800 students. (6) The Warsaw Higher School of Political Economy is also a registered private school.

Low Living Expenses

Living expenses in Poland are quite low, especially for students. It is easy to find accommodation in major cities. The Academic Home has rooms for one, two, four, or six people to live in. It is also possible to live in private homes. The monthly cost of board and lodging is equivalent to 75 Chinese dollars. Living expenses in Warsaw are more expensive, while Wilno is cheaper. As for expenses, if calculated at 200 Slola per month, the annual cost is only 1,200 Chinese dollars.

Duration and Degrees

Those who study law need an average of about four years. After passing the final examination, they are awarded a Magister of Low degree. To obtain a doctorate, they must write another thesis after obtaining this degree. Those who study medicine must study for more than five years, and after passing the examination, they are awarded the degree of doctor. Higher specialized schools must study for at least five to seven years before awarding an engineering degree. The courses at the Higher School of Commerce take about four years to complete. The courses at the Higher School of Agriculture take about three years to complete. After passing the examination, they are awarded an agricultural engineering degree.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (98) 177

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

After he was seated and the room was quiet, Mrs. Jo, who was sitting nearby showing Demi picture cards, said in a concerned tone, while nodding towards the various treasures still in Don's hands:

"Where did you learn so much about these things?"

"I've always loved these things, but I didn't know much about them. Fortunately, I met Mr. Hyde, and he told me so much."

"Who is Mr. Hyde?"

"Oh, he lives in the woods and studies these things - I don't know what you call him - writing about fish and other things. He lives at Mr. Bay's place and often asks me to help him. It's very interesting because he tells me so much, and he's a very pleasant and smart person. I hope I can see him again someday."

Mrs. Jo also said, "I hope you will," because Don's eyes had already lit up, and he was enthusiastically discussing this matter, reversing his usual quiet and reserved state.

"Oh, he can get birds to come to him, and rabbits and squirrels don't avoid him at all, as if he were a tree. He never hurts them, and they seem to recognize him. Have you ever tickled a lizard with a piece of grass?" Don suddenly asked eagerly.

"No, but I'd like to try it."

"Oh, I've done it. It's so funny to watch them stretch out their bodies and turn around. They like you doing that. Mr. Hyde often does that; he whistles to attract snakes to listen to him. He knows exactly when that flower will bloom, and bees won't sting him. He knows many wonderful things about fish, flies, aborigines, rocks, etc."

Economic Supplement

A Review of China's Tung Oil Foreign Trade 178

— Li Junsi

I

Tung oil is originally a special product of China and an indispensable raw material for the paint industry. In recent years, on the one hand, the silk and tea, which used to occupy an important position in the country's export trade, have gradually declined. On the other hand, due to the urgent need for tung oil in various countries around the world, the export of tung oil has rapidly increased. Especially in recent years, its significant progress in international trade has not only kept pace with silk, tea, and other commodities, ranking among the important ones, but also seems to have a tendency to rise and replace them. For example, in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the total export quantity of the four major commodities of silk, tea, summer cloth, and tung oil was 1,806,033 dan, while the export quantity of tung oil was 1,246,847 dan, accounting for more than 69% of the total. In terms of value, the total export value of the four major commodities was 85,594,922 yuan, of which the export value of tung oil was 30,261,269 yuan, accounting for more than 35% of the total value. From this, it can be seen that the foreign trade of tung oil is no less than that of silk and tea. Under the annual huge trade deficit and the universal decline in foreign trade of various commodities, this phenomenon is not unwelcome and can be used as a way to fill part of the trade deficit. In the international trade war, is it possible to maintain its forward momentum permanently? Undoubtedly, these are all issues worthy of our attention. The task of this article is to provide a considerable review of these issues in order to understand its current situation and future prospects.

II

Before we examine the current situation of tung oil foreign trade, we must first conduct a simple review of its past.

The foreign trade of tung oil in China started in the mid-19th century. As early as the eighth year of Tongzhi (1869), tung oil was first shipped to the United States. However, the quantity exported at that time was small and the value was low, so it did not attract general attention. However, the paint industry in various countries gradually developed, and the use of industrial raw materials became increasingly widespread. Therefore, by the seventh year of the Republic of China, there were 16 places in the world selling tung oil from China. By the ninth year of the Republic, it had expanded to 18 places. As of the year before last, 26 countries needed tung oil from China, but the quantities varied. The United States, Hong Kong, the United Kingdom, the Netherlands, Denmark, Germany, France, Belgium, Italy, Norway, Japan, as well as Australia, Korea, and the leased territory of Kwantung, are the main countries exporting tung oil from China. Under this circumstance, as the foreign market for tung oil gradually expanded, and the demand from various countries gradually increased, the corresponding increase in the export of tung oil was inevitable. Therefore, China's foreign trade in tung oil is developing at a high speed. If we compare the highest export value in the 19th year of the Republic of China with the export value of tung oil during the Tongzhi period, we don’t know how many times it has differed. Even compared with the export value of the first year of the Republic of China, it is incomparable. We can understand the increasing trend of tung oil exports by looking at the following table. In this table, we see that since the first year of the Republic of China, the export of tung oil has not permanently maintained an upward trend, and there have been significant declines in between. However, if we try to list the sum of the quantity and value of its exports from the first year of the Republic of China to the twentieth year of the Republic of China in five-year periods, then its rapid progress can be clearly demonstrated:

Tung Oil Export Statistics for the Past 23 Years

Quantity (Dan) Value (Yuan)

Republic of China Year 1 585,815 8,734,806

Year 2 453,674 6,002,254

Year 3 438,876 5,604,412

Year 4 310,344 4,518,514

Year 5 515,173 8,267,127

Total 2,303,882 33,127,113

Year 6 401,361 7,253,862

Year 7 488,852 8,953,889

Year 8 613,455 2,941,452

Year 9 540,716 10,108,787

Year 10 419,549 8,198,645

Total 2,463,933 46,456,635

Year 11 745,565 16,332,195

Year 12 836,897 26,216,132

Year 13 796,038 26,572,070

Year 14 894,073 26,175,156

Year 15 748,184 22,443,470

Total 4,020,757 107,739

Year 16 910,294 32,996,421

Year 17 1,094,299 34,953,339

Year 18 1,069,650 35,279,553

Year 19 1,167,255 48,820,308

Year 20 864,864 28,814,177

Total 5,106,361 180,823,798

Year 21 802,769 23,161,232

Year 22 1,246,847 30,061,169

Year 23 652,8 36,036,683

(Quintals)

In the above table, we can also see that since the 15th year of the Republic of China, the value of tung oil exported from China has shown a rising trend. Overall, in these five years, it has more than doubled. However, since the 20th year of the Republic of China, it has been fluctuating, far less than in the 19th year. The reason is that the Yangtze River basin suffered a major flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China, which greatly affected the tung oil production area, so the output of tung oil decreased sharply. In terms of trade, it showed a sharp decline. By the 21st year of the Republic of China, inheriting the aftermath of last year's flood, production was even lower, and trade became even more sluggish. Until the summer of the 22nd year, because the United States abandoned the gold standard, all prices rose, and the United States was the largest customer for tung oil from China, so the inland oil mills increased production, resulting in a large increase in output and smooth sales. However, by the 23rd year, the figures declined again due to the general economic downturn in the world and the difficulty in exporting Chinese goods due to the increase in silver prices in the United States.

However, since this year, the foreign trade of tung oil seems to have a revitalized outlook, and in terms of figures, there are remarkable achievements. According to the statistics of the International Trade Herald, the export of tung oil in the first half of this year accounted for the largest (June) 10.9% and the smallest (February) 4.2% of the total value of monthly local product exports. In the six months from January to June, March, April, May and June ranked first in foreign exports, and did not reach the high and low levels of the 19th year.

III

Although the foreign trade of tung oil has had a relatively prosperous development recently, and the future seems to have unlimited hope, we should consider whether its management methods are reasonable? Whether there is consistent contact in terms of transactions? Whether the method of tung oil extraction is scientific? Whether there are adequate facilities for domestic transportation? We can find that the organization of tung oil trade is entirely built on an unsound foundation, and there are great internal contradictions. Regarding this, we can examine it from two aspects:

(1) Extraction and refining - Regarding extraction, there is no need to say that the method of extracting tung oil in China, like everything else, is sticking to the old ways. The procedures for extracting tung oil are roughly as follows: first, the tung seeds are picked from the tung tree, peeled off the outer shell, washed with clean water, dried in the sun, and after drying, ground into fine powder. Then, they are placed in a wooden steamer for steaming. After steaming for about half an hour, they are taken out and placed in a hoop, wrapped in hemp cloth, made into a cake shape, and then placed in a press to extract the oil. Under high pressure, liquid will flow out of the press, and this flowing out is the tung oil. However, the tung oil extracted by this old method must go through batches of procedures and pass through many unclean utensils. Let’s not talk about the deliberate adulteration of miscellaneous oils by unscrupulous merchants to reduce the quality. Even if ordinary legitimate merchants try their best to maintain its purity and improve its quality, it is undoubtedly extremely difficult under such circumstances. In this way, the old method of oil extraction, which is individually operated and cannot be expanded to large-scale collective operation, often makes the quality and grade of the extracted oil inconsistent and fail to meet the standards. Therefore, it is easy to have a negative impact on the reputation in international trade. For this reason, tung oil sold abroad must generally be refined again after extraction to improve its quality. But when it comes to the refining of tung oil, it is really a huge stain in the history of tung oil trade. The fact is that since China's tung oil foreign trade started, it has not even had an oil refinery, so it has to rely on foreigners, because foreign oil refineries are not lacking in China. The oil refineries operated by foreigners in China are mostly concentrated in Hankou. Among these many factories, the largest is undoubtedly the American firm Qi Lai Yanghang. The oil tank of Qi Lai Yanghang can hold 3,500 tons of tung oil at a time. The second largest is the oil tank of Mobil Oil Refinery, which also has a capacity of 1,500 tons. Other foreign firms such as Mitsui and Mitsubishi of Japan, Anli and Jardine Matheson of the United Kingdom all have oil refining equipment. Although the capacity is smaller, it can refine an average of more than 1,000 tons of oil. Not long ago, Jardine Matheson established a small-scale oil refining pond in Yichang with a capacity of about 100 tons, which was very convenient for local oil merchants. Because once the tung oil is put into the pond for refining, the moisture in the oil is extracted by steam method, and the slag is also precipitated. Not only is the oil clean and transparent, but also the color is pure yellow, and the quality of tung oil can be improved a lot. But unfortunately, the establishment of each oil refinery is all foreign capital.

(2) Transportation Regarding transportation, the overseas transportation of tung oil exported abroad is beyond our reach and need not be discussed. Even domestic transportation must rely on foreigners, which has to be said to be a painful thing. We know that the tung-producing areas in China include Jiangsu, Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi and other provinces, with an area of no less than tens of thousands of square miles. Among the shipments of tung oil from these provinces, except for Guangdong and Guangxi, which are centered on Hong Kong, and Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangsu, which are centered on Shanghai, the tung oil from Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, Shaanxi, Guizhou, and Yunnan are mostly concentrated in the two ports of Wanxian and Hankou. Chongqing, Yichang, Changsha and other places have invisibly become distribution centers for tung oil. Because tung oil is collected sporadically from inland villages and towns, it must be transported to the distribution centers to wait for loading. For example, tung oil from western Sichuan is concentrated in Chongqing, and then transshipped to Wanxian or Hankou, and then sold to foreign merchants or shipped abroad. The ordinary freight from Chongqing to Hankou is 20 yuan per ton, and it only costs about 10 yuan from Yichang to Hankou. But the ships we see transporting tung oil are all foreign ships. There are very few Chinese merchant ships. why? Because tung oil is not like other dry cargo, the transporting ships must have oil tank equipment, but none of the Chinese Yangtze River steamships have this equipment, so tung oil merchants have to resort to foreign ships. However, several years ago, foreign ships did not have this oil tank equipment, so tung oil transportation had to be transshipped in Yichang and transferred to the tung oil iron barges of Taikoo and Jardine Matheson. However, foreign capital is strong and farsighted. Seeing that tung oil is the main cargo of Yangtze River freight, the quantity needed to be transported is large, and the profit is also large, so the newly built ships are specially equipped with oil tanks in order to monopolize the transportation of tung oil. This formed a situation in which foreign ships manipulated the transportation of tung oil. Under this circumstance, foreign ships often arbitrarily increase freight rates, which increases the cost of tung oil. The increase in the cost of tung oil often has a negative impact on foreign exports.

From the above two points, we can see that except for planting, most of the operation of tung oil is entrusted to foreigners. So, is the rise of this commodity to an important position in export trade a sound development? Are the tens of millions of transactions each year falling into the hands of the Chinese? Needless to say, it is already clear!

IV

From the previous section, we have understood that the so-called foreign trade of tung oil, which occupies an important position in China's local product exports, is originally manipulated by foreign merchants. In this section, we will look forward to its future.

According to factual reports, we know that since tung oil was first exported to the United States, the United States has always been the largest customer in China's tung oil trade. Not to mention the past, even looking at recent years, its position is becoming increasingly important, which is a very obvious fact. The following table shows the percentage of Chinese tung oil exported to the United States in the total number in the past six years:

Year Export Total Index Number of Dan Imported to the United States Percentage

Republic of China Year 18 1,069,650 735,244 68.7

Year 19 1,167,255 874,006 75.0

Year 20 864,864 549,600 63.5

Year 21 802,669 495,792 60.4

Year 22 1,246,847 899,100 70.5

Year 23 115,826 410,190 65.5

(Quintals) (Quintals)

From the above table, it can be seen that the average annual tung oil shipped to the United States accounts for about 70% of the total. Since the United States accounts for such a huge proportion, if it suddenly does not use tung oil from China, China will suddenly lose a very large customer. Although there are still 30% of the customers, it will inevitably fall into a bleak and sluggish state, and it is impossible to avoid this result. Moreover, at this time, it is still doubtful whether this 30% of the customers can be maintained. Therefore, in the tung oil trade, the United States and China have a very close relationship. But let's see what attitude the United States government and the public hold towards using tung oil from China. Of course, tung oil has become an indispensable raw material in industry today, and it has to continue to purchase from China for the time being. However, on the other hand, in order to prevent the huge annual leakage, almost the entire country is enthusiastically promoting tung tree planting. According to general estimates, each acre of tung trees can produce two tons of tung fruit. If the selling price per ton is 20-25 yuan, then each acre can earn 40-50 yuan, which is more profitable than growing coffee. Moreover, there are also oil cake and other income. At the same time, after the tung fruit is sold to the factory, the factory can still make a lot of profit, because assuming the price of tung is 15 yuan per ton, and its oil content is 20%, then the price of tung oil per pound after extraction is only 5-6 cents, which is 3-4 cents more than the current market price of 8-10 cents. In practice, if the manufacturing methods of the factory are more precise and the distribution management is more scientific, the gains will be even greater. Therefore, the United States government and the public are actively building large-scale factories and enthusiastically promoting tung tree planting. Although most of the provinces have not achieved good results, Florida has expanded from 20,000 acres of tung trees planted in 1924 to 40,000 acres, and the number of tung trees has reached 4 million, which is undoubtedly a huge threat to the future of China's tung oil trade.

At the same time, we see that other countries that account for the top three of China's tung oil exports are also enthusiastically promoting tung tree planting, just like the United States. In the United Kingdom, since the Oil Consultant Committee of the Royal Society and the paint industrialists cooperated to purchase a large number of tung seeds from China and the United States, they have distributed them to various territories for trial planting. According to recent reports, Australia, New Zealand, India, Burma, Ceylon, Malaya, the Union of South Africa, Sudan, the West Indies, Honduras, and other British territories have achieved considerable results, and the future is still limitless. In addition, all aspects have achieved good results: Argentina has planted 50,000 tung trees, Paraguay has planted 30,000 tung trees, and Russia has planted 900 acres. It is now planning to plant 36,000 acres of tung trees in 1937. Other countries such as Italy and Central and South American countries have purchased a large number of tung seeds from the United States for trial planting. But? We know that the growth of tung trees to oil extraction requires a lot of time, so at present, it is not easy for countries around the world to achieve self-sufficiency in tung oil. Therefore, China's foreign trade in tung oil will not be abandoned in the international market for a while. However, in the near future, after the tung tree planting business in various countries is effective, they will collect their own seeds for oil extraction and no longer need to purchase from China. This is an inevitable fact. At that time, China's foreign exports of tung oil will inevitably deteriorate and fall into a tragic situation. Hundreds of thousands of people across the country who directly and indirectly depend on tung tree planting will inevitably be severely affected, because China's own tung oil demand is very limited, and most of the tung oil is prepared for export abroad.

In the end, I have to say: the reason why China's tung oil has a special development is nothing more than taking advantage of geographical advantages! Because the soil and climate in the southern part of China are most suitable for planting tung trees, and the most developed are those planted in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and the Guijiang River basin. However, this advantage of natural geography will become a historical relic and gradually fail. However, we must not be discouraged. We must use this advantage of natural geography to select good varieties and eliminate inferior varieties on the one hand, and use scientific methods to extract and refine oil to reduce costs on the other hand. As for improving transportation and establishing close contact with the financial community, it is an indispensable task. In short, whether China's tung oil can permanently maintain its glorious position in the world market and not become a sequel to silk and tea depends entirely on the Chinese people's rapid pursuit and determination to improve and make prior rescues.

Inside Story of the Global Crude Oil Struggle 179

— Nai Gong

More than sixty years ago, crude oil was only used for treating women's cancer. But now, whether in industry, transportation, or especially in the military, crude oil has become an indispensable protagonist. During the European War, the French "Tiger" Georges Clemenceau once said, "A drop of crude oil is as precious as a drop of blood." No wonder there have been many disputes among countries recently, with the crude oil issue as their focus. Examples include the exploitation of crude oil in Northern Sakhalin by Japan and Russia, and the issue of concessions for oil fields in Abyssinia.

Regarding the production, use, and extraction technology of crude oil, many scholars in China have provided detailed introductions. What this article describes now is the inside story of the crude oil struggle among various countries. On the one hand, we can see the acuteness of the competition for crude oil among countries; at the same time, we can see that they have grand plans and steps for everything, unlike China, which lacks foresight.

(1) The Seizure of the Persian Crude Oil Mining Rights

More than twenty years before the European War, the Persian King Naser al-Din Shah Qajar was never willing to provide assistance to Europeans and Americans. He only allowed a small number of Europeans to travel within Persia. At that time, Canadian engineer William Knox D'Arcy was one of them. D'Arcy knew that in the past, near many churches in Persia, there were often eternal sacred flames; and on the opposite shore of the Caspian Sea, Russia had already been engaged in crude oil extraction; therefore, he concluded that Persia must have crude oil mines, so he decided to explore on the ground.

D'Arcy traveled all over Persia, but he never found what he was looking for. He lost a lot of money, but he did not lose his faith in himself or his faith in God. During his travels, in addition to carrying necessary equipment, maps, and books, he also carried images of Jesus and the Bible. Later, the money lost reached as much as 10 million francs; his spirit and perseverance made British financiers very excited, so they provided D'Arcy with financial assistance. However, the crude oil mine was never found, and the British financiers treated D'Arcy with contempt; therefore, D'Arcy also became disheartened.

D'Arcy stopped searching for oil fields and instead helped the Persian king develop various businesses. He built a short railway and also engaged in machinery trade. In 1901, the Persian king granted him a "Charter." In the "Charter," the king allowed D'Arcy and his followers and successors the freedom to explore and exploit any minerals in Persia for seventy years. Regardless of whether minerals were discovered or not, the "Charter" itself already had great value. At the same time, just as this "Charter" was being granted, D'Arcy received a report that crude oil mines had been discovered in Shushtar, southern Persia. D'Arcy felt very happy. People used to call him a Utopian idealist, but now he could prove the correctness of his beliefs.

However, D'Arcy no longer had the willingness and courage to operate the oil mine. He wanted to return to England and spend his remaining years. Someone offered one million pounds sterling to buy his "Charter," but he was unwilling. Later, it was increased to six million pounds sterling, but D'Arcy was still unmoved. He recalled his life, the indifference of London financiers towards him, and the Persian king's favor towards him. He was unwilling for Persia to become a place for others to compete. He was old and no longer had any hope in life. He only wanted to rest and spend his remaining years leisurely. At this time, D'Arcy was surrounded by merchants and detectives who wanted to obtain this "Charter." So he secretly took a boat to the United States, hoping to return to Canada.

On the ship, D'Arcy absolutely did not talk to anyone. He prayed to God and read the Bible. When the ship passed through Africa, a clergyman also took this ship to the United States. Later, D'Arcy gradually became acquainted with this clergyman and told him about his attachment to Persia and his willingness to pray for Persia. When the ship was two days away from New York, D'Arcy told the clergyman all about his life, the Persian king's favor towards him, and the granting of the "Charter." This clergyman listened to D'Arcy's words without saying a word, seeming not very interested. Later, he suddenly said to D'Arcy, "Why don't you give this 'Charter' to the church? On the one hand, it can avoid disputes, and on the other hand, the church can preach in Persia after obtaining the 'Charter'." D'Arcy did not answer at the time, but before the ship arrived in New York Harbor, he gave this "Charter" to the clergyman and transferred it to the church. This clergyman's name was Sidney Reilly. He was not a missionary clergyman, but an agent sent by the British Admiralty. This "Charter" from Reilly was given to the British Admiralty. The "Charter" that could not be purchased for six million pounds sterling was obtained by an agent of the British Admiralty without spending a penny. In 1914, 56% of the shares of the Anglo-Persian Oil Company were controlled by the British Admiralty. This secret was initially hidden until the outbreak of the war, when it was revealed.

(2) The Crude Oil Dispute between Britain and the United States

Since Britain had obtained the Persian oil fields, it aroused Russia's jealousy. As a result, Persia divided the country's crude oil mines into two zones: the north was given to Russia, and the south was given to Britain. On the British side, they felt quite dissatisfied, so they used spies and various extraordinary methods. Later, all the oil fields in Persia were still completely returned to Britain. The person in charge of this activity was not British, but Dutch. His contribution to Britain was greater than that of the average Englishman. He was a cornerstone in maintaining British interests. This is Henry Deterding, the current general manager of Royal Dutch.

Deterding was originally the manager of a small crude oil company in the Dutch East Indies. In the Dutch East Indies, he met Kessler, the general manager of Royal Dutch at the time. Kessler appreciated him very much. He publicly said to people, "Deterding alone is worth ten billion pounds sterling," so he hired him to work at Royal Dutch. At this time, the company's finances were very difficult. Kessler and Deterding tried to increase capital, but they only raised 500,000 Dutch guilders. In this precarious situation, Royal Dutch obtained many very large crude oil mines. The company's business was booming again. This aroused the jealousy of Rockefeller's Standard Oil Company and began to attack this British-Dutch group. Many shareholders of Royal Dutch agreed to sell the company to the Americans. But Deterding resolutely opposed it. At that time, Kessler, the general manager of Royal Dutch, was critically ill, and he strongly supported Deterding to take his place. The shareholders followed Kessler's wishes and asked Deterding to serve as general manager.

With a capital of 500 Dutch guilders, Deterding declared war on Rockefeller, who had hundreds of millions of assets. Fortunately, he allied with Marcus Samuel, and only then was he able to win the war. Samuel was initially a low-level employee of a shipping company. Later, he saved some capital and bought an old ship. Because the business developed, he increased to twelve new-style ships. He transported goods from the Far East to Europe, but the goods transported back from Europe were very few. Someone suggested that when the ships sailed back from Europe to the Far East, they could conveniently transport Persian crude oil to India. He suddenly felt that transporting crude oil was a very important business. So he allocated a lot of capital to build crude oil ships. He not only engaged in transporting crude oil, but also mined crude oil. Before he joined hands with Deterding, they were actually in a position of mutual competition.

Deterding had abundant crude oil mines, and Samuel had a large number of crude oil transport ships. They decided to unite and form a united front, with one specializing in production and the other specializing in transportation. In 1902, they organized the Asiatic Petroleum Company, specializing in crude oil trade.

Rockefeller's first strategic step was to blockade crude oil ships. He was willing to let empty ships stop sailing rather than transport Royal Dutch's crude oil. Standard Oil had 200,000 kilometers of pipelines in the United States, and the pipeline transportation fee was only one-sixteenth of the railway transportation fee. Therefore, many small crude oil companies in the United States could not compete with Standard Oil. Rockefeller also wanted to use the same method to deal with Royal Dutch, but he already had Samuel's oil tankers to handle transportation for him, so Rockefeller's first plan failed.

Since the transportation blockade policy failed, a price war began. The battlefield this time was in China. China had 400 million people, and Rockefeller considered it his excellent market. He lowered the price of crude oil below cost and sold it in the Chinese market. He distributed 8 million lamps to the Chinese people. But the Chinese people accepted Rockefeller's lamps but used Deterding's crude oil.

Deterding's policy was the same as Rockefeller's. He lowered the price of crude oil to a very low level and sold it in the Chinese market. But because the transportation was closer, the damage was less. Standard Oil's losses in China were offset by raising the selling price in the European and American markets. The increase in the selling price in the European market also benefited Royal Dutch. But Rockefeller's increase in the price of crude oil in the American market caused great resentment among the American people. Therefore, Deterding took advantage of this opportunity to establish a crude oil company with Rockefeller's enemies in Florida, and British crude oil forces penetrated the hinterland of the United States. Now the oil fields in California are also owned by him. Not only does he own a part of the crude oil mines in the United States, but most of the crude oil mines in Central America and South America are also controlled by Deterding.

Most geologists believe that the crude oil mines in Venezuela, South America, are the richest in the world. Here, the struggle for British and American rights is also very sharp. More than ten years ago, the British side instigated their revolution. As a result, Gomey gained power and became the president of Venezuela, while economically, he was completely supplied by Deterding. Venezuela's oil fields were entirely in Deterding's hands. All the crude oil extracted was also transported to Curaçao for refining and then transported for export.

Curaçao is a small island off the coast of Venezuela, a Dutch territory. On this island, there are oil refining facilities and navigation ports. Venezuelan crude oil would lose its function without Curaçao. The residents of the island speak a mixture of English, Portuguese, Spanish, and Dutch. They often clamor for independence because the Americans tell them that if they become independent, Curaçao's tax revenue can be used by themselves and does not have to be sent to the Netherlands. Curaçao has become an important town for British crude oil. Washington and the American oil companies are constantly trying to instigate the people on the island to resist and maintain their independence. This is not for any true meaning, but for crude oil.

Gomey is the current president of Venezuela. He has ruled for fifteen years and is a tyrannical dictator. In Venezuela, many people shout "Long live Gomey!" because Gomey supports them and allows them to live a life of luxury and leisure. Revolutions often occur in Venezuela, and the economic backing for the revolutionaries is Standard Oil.

During the European War, the need for crude oil increased even more. Because the Atlantic Ocean was attacked by submarines, Standard Oil transferred crude oil to the Far Eastern market for sales, especially China. By December 1917, France's crude oil reserves were only 28,000 tons, enough to supply the Allied forces for only two days. In an emergency, Standard Oil's crude oil was transported, allowing the Allied forces to avoid the famine of crude oil. General Ludendorff also said that the victory of the Allied Powers was due to crude oil.

(3) The New Lineup of Soviet Russia's Crude Oil Strategy

Since Britain obtained the Persian crude oil mining rights, the secret struggle between Russia and Britain in Persia has never ceased. Before the European War, the Persian king had ceded the oil fields in the north to Russia, but Britain used various methods to achieve its long-cherished wish of destruction.

Soviet Russia itself originally had very rich oil fields. Before the European War, its crude oil production was almost equal to that of the United States. In the early years after the revolution, production decreased sharply. In 1922, it was 8 million tons; but by 1933, it had increased to 38 million tons. Soviet Russia's crude oil strategy was to unite with the United States to overthrow British forces. The person in charge of this matter was Einhorn, a famous Soviet Russian intelligence operative.

Einhorn and Reza Khan, the current king of Persia, were the two protagonists in overthrowing British forces in Persia. They used Russia's power to obtain independence for Persia from the status of a British protectorate. In 1928, Persia announced that all foreign privileges in Persia were completely abolished. In 1932, Persia abolished the crude oil monopoly. In 1933, Persia and the Anglo-Persian Oil Company signed a new contract to replace the "Charter" obtained by D'Arcy in 1901. In the new contract, Persia did not lease all the oil fields to Britain. The company had to give the government 20% of the profits each year. Moreover, for every ton of crude oil extracted, a tax of 9 was required. Moreover, other minerals were not included in the lease. From then on, D'Arcy's "Charter" became waste paper. Britain's crude oil base and all its forces in Persia were completely lost.

In 1927, Deterding wanted to blockade Soviet Russia's foreign market for crude oil, causing extreme panic in Soviet Russia. So Standard Oil purchased a large amount of Russian oil and sold it at a lower price in the British crude oil market, causing Deterding to suffer huge losses. This competition ended only when Hoover was elected president. Now, Standard Oil and the Soviet Russian side are still cooperating, and Standard Oil's intelligence operatives are also in close contact with the Soviet Russian crude oil operatives.

(4) The Mystery of Harding and Rivera

In 1920, Harding was elected president of the United States with the economic backing of Rockefeller. He was almost a blind tool of Standard Oil, and he agreed to everything that was asked of him. Later, he felt that this puppet was quite improper, and the company's demands were excessive, so Harding gradually changed his attitude. In the early summer of 1923, he openly opposed Standard Oil. In the summer of the same year, he left Washington for summer vacation. Later, news came from Vancouver that President Harding had suddenly died violently. Some said that he was poisoned by insects, some said that he was murdered by a woman, and some had other guesses, but it seems that they forgot that he was very likely to have sacrificed for crude oil.

In 1927, Primo de Rivera was the dictator of Spain. He expelled the Communist Party and revived Spain. He felt that the import of crude oil greatly harmed Spain's interests, so he created a crude oil monopoly system to give part of the profits to the government. This system was of course contrary to the interests of Deterding and Rockefeller. So the two of them joined forces and did not sell oil to Spain. Spain had no choice but to buy the lowest-quality crude oil at the highest price from its enemy, Soviet Russia. At the same time, the British side launched a campaign to not buy Spanish agricultural products, and the American side also increased import taxes on Spanish goods. The situation in Spain became chaotic, and Rivera's government was overthrown. He fled to Paris, but he also died suddenly not long after.

(5) Conclusion

The above is just a few scenes in the global struggle for crude oil. Countries are almost constantly thinking about crude oil. In France, it is now stipulated that crude oil must be mixed with alcohol. In Germany, crude oil is extracted from coal. Now the production of crude oil is still led by the United States, but according to the report of the Geological Survey Division of the US Department of the Interior, the consumption of crude oil in the United States is about twice the total consumption of all other countries in the world. But by 1940, the crude oil reserves in the United States will be exhausted, while the crude oil of other countries can still supply the world for 200 years. But most of the crude oil mines in the world are controlled by Britain. In other words, in five years, the United States will purchase a large amount of crude oil for its consumption from Britain. The United States controls the present of crude oil, and Britain holds the future of crude oil.

Finance: Jiangguang Coins Fell in the Gray Market 180

Yesterday was Sunday, and the financial market was relatively quiet. The foreign exchange rate was still 23 cents. Money shops collected and settled more than 48 million foreign exchange public orders, more than 400,000 remittances from various routes, and 200,000 cash from inland routes. Securities Last Week Bonds Suddenly Suffered a Setback 181

Though There Were Rallies Midway... The Final Result Was Still a Fall of Two to Three Yuan

Last week, from November 11th to 16th, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Exchange market was turbulent. Just as the currency system reform was flourishing, it suddenly suffered an unexpected blow, and a sharp decline began. This was mainly due to excessive gains, which easily triggered a reaction. Fortunately, most of the bulls were concentrated among large investors, and the shorts took the opportunity to cover their positions, so it did not lead to a market crash. The support from the three banks also provided some strength. The current environment is still unstable. Externally, the relationship between Britain and Italy is worsening, and the domestic situation is extremely complex, which is unlikely to end in the short term. Moreover, the accumulated amount of public bonds is enormous, and the November futures have only a few days left. The environment is precarious, and there will inevitably be another drastic change. Reviewing the past week, the Japanese naval incident in Hongkou occurred on Monday. Although sellers surged, buyers were also strong, and market prices fluctuated constantly. There were both highs and lows, and the bulls tried their best to push up the 96 bonds to mislead the public, which was nothing more than a speculative strategy to cover their positions. On Tuesday, the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's birth, the market was closed for a day. On Wednesday, rumors spread, and the bulls exited the market. Numbers 47 and 48 were also sold off, leading to a sharp drop of several jiao (tenths of a yuan) to about two yuan. On Thursday, selling pressure was strongest. Numbers 47, 48, 54, and 78 were sold off continuously. The closing price of the Sixth National Loan barely avoided a limit-down by one jiao. On Friday, there were rumors of support from the three banks to maintain the market. Whether this was true could not be verified. Numbers 46 and 78, etc., were indeed bought, but it was unclear whether they were absorbing at low prices under this guise. The shorts could only avoid their sharp edge, and retail investors were exhausted from running around. As a result, market prices reversed direction, with highs and lows varying considerably. On Saturday, the bullish momentum was still strong, with both markets rising nearly three yuan. The closing price only recovered slightly, rising from a few jiao to 1.67 yuan. Currently, the market price differs from the previous week's highest price by no more than four yuan, and the Sixth National Loan differs by less than one yuan, almost reaching the previous high, which is likely unsustainable given the overall environment. In conclusion, the situation is fraught with incidents, and the bond market is still at a high peak. The future is not optimistic. The market price for the week ended with a drop of approximately one yuan to 3.30 yuan. The total transaction volume was 16,800 units, amounting to 145,000 yuan. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 185

— (Yu Mugu)

All disputes and problems in the world, if based on true justice, will have true right and wrong. No matter how complicated the dispute is, it can be easily resolved. It is just that the powerful do not consider justice themselves, but insist that others follow their inexplicable and incomprehensible barbarous justice. Therefore, true right and wrong are obliterated, and the disturbance becomes even worse.

When beasts fight each other for hunger, at most, both sides will be injured. We criticize them for being cruel, but the cruelty of human beings is a thousand times greater than that of beasts fighting each other. Look at how people usually promote humanitarianism and maintain the peaceful and kind nature of a false mask. However, in the name of maintaining peace and self-defense, they secretly calculate plans to kill and rush to make lethal weapons. When the wild nature erupts one day, they use all possible cruel methods of fighting and killing.

The parties involved, the related parties, the lawyers on both sides, and the judges, when interrogating and debating, the various postures of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness are faster than the changes of wind and clouds. If you use a fast-motion camera to continuously capture the postures of each person during a single interrogation period, the strange and bizarre appearances will definitely be spectacular and can arouse the endless research interest of philosophers and psychologists.

Concessions 186

— Yang Yusheng

I once heard a joke. It said that a blind person could judge "Chinese territory" and "foreign territory" based on the feeling of the nerves in the soles of his feet, because the former is mostly gravel roads, uneven in height, while the latter is paved with asphalt roads.

The so-called "foreign territory" refers to the general term for concessions. Shanghainese people use terms such as "Great British Territory" and "French Territory," and they seem to forget the sovereignty of those lands! This should be strictly corrected.

It seems that the term "concession" cannot be found between large and small countries in Europe and the United States, but it is particularly connected with us Chinese. It is signed for ninety-nine years, or even leased indefinitely. It really has the spirit of "growing old together for a hundred years"!

Yokohama, Japan, was once opened as a trading port and established a concession in 1859, but it was immediately taken back after the Meiji Restoration. Their method of abolishing the concession relied entirely on the natural movements of the people. Wherever the areas adjacent to the concession were, the roads were particularly wide, the houses were particularly neat, the transportation was particularly convenient, and public facilities such as electric lights, tap water, parks, museums, libraries, and educational institutions such as kindergartens and schools were all particularly exquisite! Striving for perfection! So that people have no intention of running to the concession! It is said that the relics of this kind of "hard work in construction" and "peaceful struggle" can still be seen very clearly! It is by relying on this spirit of continuous self-improvement that they can get rid of all shackles and progress day by day.

This is a great mirror for us Chinese. Even today, if everyone is still thinking about going to the concession to make foreign money, seek comfort, and indulge in pleasure, without some revitalizing spirit and the concept of becoming strong, then, not to mention that there is no time limit for the current concession to be returned! Even all the land in the country will inevitably have a day when it is "leased" entirely!

Effective Treatment for Jealousy 187

— Sun Linchang

Jealousy is a characteristic of human beings, especially in women. That's why there is a place name in northern China called "Yidufu Ferry". It is said that in ancient times, there was a Cang Geng who could cure this disease. According to the research results of French medical doctor Fale, this kind of jealousy is caused by a kind of endocrine in the human body. Endocrine is the most magical in the human body. If a person's endocrine has not fully developed, then that person's body must be short and small, because endocrine is the main thing that stimulates human physiology, and it cannot be neglected. Endocrine is particularly developed during adolescence, so jealousy is also the most intense. In recent times, young men and women are caught up in love triangles and create waves in the sea of vinegar, which is unmanageable; according to Lei Shi, "it is all caused by jealousy." Now, based on the above principles, Lei Shi has invented a special medicine that shrinks the endocrine. Once injected, the excitement of the endocrine will decline, and the heart of jealousy will also disappear.
